The Japanese Kwantung Army Annexes All Industries in Manchuria; The Result of the Restructuring of the South Manchuria Railway Company 41

(Changchun) As a result of consultations with various parties, the Vice President of the South Manchuria Railway Company, Hatta, the Chief of Staff of the Kwantung Army, Isoya, and the authorities of "Manchukuo" will consolidate all industries in Manchuria, such as railways, coal mines, iron manufacturing, light metals, oil, and electricity, to create a general company for a controlled economy. This restructuring plan has been agreed upon by the South Manchuria Railway Company, the Kwantung Army, and "Manchukuo", with a completely unified attitude. What remains is the railway issue. It is proposed to combine the aforementioned industries into a company, follow the "Manchukuo Government" organizational law, be managed by the Ministry of Industry, and form a "Manchukuo" corporation. The fundamental policy is to make the company a unified inclusion of all similar industries and give it a monopoly position. The result of the discussion has been satisfactorily resolved. The Vice President of the South Manchuria Railway Company, Hatta, has returned to Dalian and reported the above situation to the board of directors. He will immediately go to Tokyo to report to the supervisory authorities. At the same time, the Chief of Staff of the Kwantung Army, Isoya, will also return to Japan to report to the military headquarters. The relevant departments of the central government will convene a joint meeting to make the final decision, and the various preparations will be made into a plan to be submitted to the next session of the Diet for passage. In this way, it can be implemented in the spring of next year and become a major reform in the history of the South Manchuria Railway Company. It is also heard that the total capital of the new company is expected to exceed 2 billion yuan. (Japan United Press dispatch on the 7th)

(Changchun) At the meeting between Chief of Staff Isoya and Vice President Hatta on the 6th, an agreement was reached on the restructuring of the South Manchuria Railway Company, which will soon be presented to the central government. The contents are currently kept strictly secret. It is reported that the main points are as follows: (1) In order to study Japan's policy towards Manchuria, it should be carried out by the Commander of the Kwantung Army as the central organization. Therefore, the South Manchuria Railway Company, which develops the economic artery of Manchuria and Mongolia, must be removed from the hands of the Colonization Ministry and placed under the unified supervision of the Commander. The various businesses of the South Manchuria Railway Company should be separated and reorganized into special companies. The capital of Xiangtie will remain at the current 800 million yuan, and the necessary capital from the mainland should be absorbed and invested in the various branch companies. The departments of railways, coal mines, and commerce, which have been separated, will be accepted by established companies, such as Showa Steel Works, Manchuria Chemical Industry Company, Telegraph and Telephone Company, Mining Company, Datong Electric Company, Light Metals Company, and Petroleum Company. The capital control of the holding companies, except for the holding companies and railways, will be the legal organization of "Manchukuo", subject to the supervision of the Military Commander and "Manchukuo". (2) The local departments will temporarily be affiliated businesses of the holding companies and will continue to manage the affiliated territory as before. When deemed appropriate, they will be transferred to Manchuria. Approximately at the time when Japan abolishes extraterritorial rights, "Manchukuo" is currently considering expenses. (3) The Military Department and the Economic Research Association of the South Manchuria Railway Company will jointly form the Economic Staff Headquarters as an advisory body for the economic organization control of the entire Manchuria. (Den-tsu Telegram on the 7th)

The Inevitability of the Russo-Japanese War: The Arrogance of the Japanese Military and Russia's High Probability of Victory: Trotsky's Observations 45

(Paris) Today, the Paris News published an important article by Trotsky titled "The Current Revolution in Japan." The article elaborates on the current animosity between Japan and Russia and speculates on the outcome of a future conflict between the two countries. According to Trotsky's analysis, the victory in a future war will ultimately belong to the Soviet Union. This is because Russia has not only undergone a complete revolution, but the potential power of the entire nation has also been awakened, allowing it to pour its immense driving force onto the battlefield. Moreover, Japan has not made significant progress since its last victory over Tsarist Russia. Trotsky further stated that the living standards of the Japanese people are lower than those of the Soviet Union, while the Soviet Union's industrial resources far surpass those of Japan. Furthermore, the Soviet Union has focused on developing heavy industry, while Japan has focused primarily on light industry. In terms of the physical constitution of the people, the comparison is also unfavorable to Japan. The arrogance of the Japanese military is entirely based on the Prussian military model, borrowing all its flaws without gaining any of its advantages. The natural qualities and individuality of Japanese soldiers, which they relied on to defeat China and Russia, such as individual initiative, focus, and the tenacity to bear personal responsibility, have been completely swept away in today's Japanese military. Trotsky concluded by saying that he did not wish to see a war break out between Russia and Japan. However, according to his observations, both a Russo-Japanese war and a US-Japanese war are within the realm of possibility. (6th National Telegraph)

On the Pacific Ocean: Large-Scale US Naval Exercises: Imagining Japan as the Enemy: In Addition to the Participation of All Warships, More Than 300 Aircraft Provide Support 46

San Pedro, California - Rear Admiral Cyrus Cole announced today that the US Navy will hold its largest mock battle in recent years next Monday and Tuesday. The entire Pacific Fleet will actually participate. The purpose of this exercise is to test the progress made in tactics by the battle fleet and patrol fleet after a year of exercises at various key ports along the Pacific coast. The location of this operation will be outside the Golden Gate of San Francisco, which is not only the most heavily defended area on the Pacific coast but also the commercial hub of the Pacific coast. In the event of war, it would be a primary target for the enemy, so it was chosen as the site for the mock battle. According to Cole's announcement, in addition to 100 surface warships, all available submarines and more than 300 aircraft, as well as the airship Macon, will participate. This is truly a large-scale exercise on the surface, underwater, and in the sky. It is also the most important demonstration of naval effectiveness before the US fleet sets sail for patrol in the Atlantic next spring. While Cole was announcing the mock battle plan, news from Washington arrived stating that Rear Admiral Standley was also announcing a shipbuilding plan for the next few years in Washington. It is said that next spring, the Navy will ask Congress to approve sufficient funds to build new ships, aiming to reach the strength permitted by the London Treaty by 1939. They will also ask Congress for a guarantee that all old ships that need to be replaced will be replaced during this period and in the years thereafter. Currently, senior naval officers are completely satisfied with the strength permitted by the London Treaty but insist on maintaining maximum effectiveness. (6th National Telegraph)

German Socialist Party Handles General Election Single-Handedly: List of Candidates Prepared: Hitler's Name is Listed First: Foreign Minister Neurath Delivers a Speech: Reiterates Desire for Peace and Demands for Equality in Armaments 52

(Berlin) - There is only one list of candidates for the November 12th general election. This list contains the names of 676 candidates. Premier Hitler is listed first, followed by nine key figures in the National Socialist Party, and then the members of the National Socialist Party caucus in the former House of Representatives, the leaders of the National Socialist Party's various branches, and the labor leaders. Among the candidates are Hitler's confidant Rosenberg, Count Reventlow, former imperial son Prince August Wilhelm, former Austrian National Socialist Party Inspector Pross, former National Socialist Party propagandist Hapscht, who was expelled from Austria and returned to Germany, and labor front leader Dr. Ley, etc. Among the former members of other parties other than the National Socialist Party who are listed as candidates, the German National People's Party ranks first, while the Centre Party and the Bavarian People's Party each have only one person. In addition, there are several people on the list of candidates who have not joined any political party. (7th Havas Telegraph)

(Berlin) - Today, German Foreign Minister Neurath delivered an important speech at the German General Assembly in Berlin, pleading in extremely earnest terms for the world's countries to understand Germany's peaceful and progressive purpose in withdrawing from the League of Nations. Regarding the upcoming general election to determine the people's support for withdrawing from the League of Nations, he said that it was an action to express Germany's feelings to the world. Germany's withdrawal from the League of Nations, firstly, cannot be regarded as an expression of Germany's resentment, and secondly, cannot be regarded as retaliation for the disarmament conference. From Germany's perspective, this action is actually a new path to progress that can achieve the goal of global harmony. Germany's withdrawal from the League of Nations has not created a crisis for the League of Nations. On the contrary, the reason why Germany must withdraw from the League of Nations is actually due to the crisis hidden and developing within the organization of the League of Nations itself, making it impossible for Germany to exist safely within it. All politicians with calm minds and true wills have recognized that there have long been ominous contradictions in the organizational foundation of the League of Nations, which on the one hand vigorously encourages idealized hopes for peace, and on the other hand still represents imperialism that has never been seen in history. In 1919, the peoples of the world were tired of turmoil, so they were overjoyed when they heard of the emergence of a permanent peace governed by justice, but these were all deceptive empty talks, and what they have obtained today is nothing more than a material organization, and its most superficial purpose is to maintain the strong position it obtained through the Treaty of Versailles, in order to perpetually oppress the defeated countries. It is indeed possible for the victorious countries to build an organization to permanently massacre and oppress the defeated countries, and it is also possible for countries to organize a common peace organization on an equal footing, but it is impossible to have both, to allow the defeated countries to be permanently oppressed, and the world to permanently maintain its peace. Neurath then listed the facts that the League of Nations was unable to be fair to Germany, and turned a blind eye to the re-occupation of the Ruhr region in 1923, and was unable to provide adequate protection to the German minority in the German colonies. Finally, he said that Germany's actions today are not a retreat but a step forward towards a practical peace policy. (6th National Telegraph)

He believes that the two countries should first exchange ambassadors, and then discuss other matters, so that they can be resolved through normal diplomatic channels. This group is using the National Recovery Administration as a shield to obscure their treacherous plans to raise prices and make profits, causing the people to sink deeper into the abyss. Currently, the retail prices of various goods are far exceeding the production costs, with the worst cases even raising prices by 63% to 120%. This price increase plan is enough to render the government's "buy now" campaign ineffective. The public, willing to buy goods at fair prices, are all backing away in the face of these outrageous prices of manufactured goods. As a result, the lack of purchasers has caused the government's unemployment relief work to lose most of its effectiveness. This group of profiteers will make the coming winter even more difficult for the poor, etc.

In previous speeches, Borah had urged the people to pay attention to efforts to resolve British war debts, saying that if war debts could be greatly reduced or completely cancelled several years ago, it would greatly benefit world trade and commerce. Chairman Chiang Adjusts Food Supply in Various Provinces, Restricts the Dumping of Foreign Rice, Reduces Grain Transportation Costs, Reduces Additional Land Taxes, Eliminates All Obstacles 95

A telegram from Nanchang reports that Chairman Chiang convened a food conference last month, attended by rice-producing provinces such as Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, and Anhui, and rice-consuming provinces and cities such as Guangdong, Shanghai, and Hebei. Detailed discussions were held on eliminating obstacles to grain circulation, seeking convenience in grain transportation and sales, and providing relief to rural finance. Yesterday, he specially submitted a request to the Central Government based on the resolutions and ordered each province to implement them one by one. The telegrams to the President of the Executive Yuan, the chairmen of the eight provincial governments, and the mayor of Shanghai are recorded separately below.

Telegram to the President of the Executive Yuan 96

Chairman Chiang telegraphed the President of the Executive Yuan, saying, "This headquarters held a food conference on the 2nd and 3rd of October, attended by representatives from ten provinces and cities including Hunan, Hubei, Henan, Anhui, Hebei, Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Jiangxi, Shanghai, and Guangdong, as well as the National Defense Design Committee. A proposal was made to reduce and eliminate difficulties in grain transportation. It was unanimously agreed that low grain prices hurt farmers and that rice prices should be increased to provide relief. However, if rice prices are to be high, obstacles must be eliminated and transportation must be facilitated so that grain is not oversupplied in one area, leading to a sharp drop in prices, while areas lacking rice face the worry of food shortages. The way to provide relief is to facilitate transportation and reduce transportation costs, which will promote circulation and reduce costs to compete with foreign rice. The main reason for the influx of foreign rice in recent years is that foreign governments encourage dumping. Foreign merchants, with the advantage of convenient transportation and low freight rates, sell at low prices and overwhelm the market. However, the opposite is true in our country. According to reports, it costs 7 jiao per 100 jin to transport rice from Wuhu to Qingdao via Shanghai, 7.4 jiao to Tianjin, 6.7 jiao to Yantai and Weihaiwei, and 6.5 jiao to Dalian. Currently, grain merchants transporting rice to Tianjin are losing several jiao to more than one yuan per bag based on current market prices due to high freight rates. The cost of transporting Wuhu rice directly to Guangzhou or Tianjin is also prohibitive. As a result, domestic rice sales are further stagnant, more foreign rice is imported, and the rural economy is increasingly impoverished. In addition to telegraphing the central government to levy heavy and rapid import duties on foreign rice, we should also ask the Ministries of Communications and Railways to instruct various shipping companies and railway bureaus to give priority to allocating ships and vehicles to those who request to transport rice, properly formulate joint transportation measures, reduce transportation procedures, and reduce freight rates to about 50% of the original price, or the government should appropriately subsidize to compensate for its additional losses, which will promote its implementation to resolve the misfortune of domestic rice. The above, etc., were resolved and recorded on file. In addition to telegraphing separately, this telegram is sent to you, hoping that you will investigate and handle it, and promptly reply with a well-defined plan on how to effectively verify and reduce freight rates and provide other conveniences. Chiang Chung-cheng"

Telegram to the Chairmen of the Eight Provinces 97

Chairman Chiang telegraphed the Chairmen of the Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hebei, and Henan Provincial Governments and the Mayor of Shanghai, (1) "It is found that this headquarters convened a food conference on the 2nd and 3rd of October, proposing to restrict additional land taxes. It was resolved that the provincial governments should be telegraphed to ensure that the additional land tax does not exceed the limit set by the Ministry of Finance, and that a thorough investigation should be made of the current collection situation in various places to effectively reduce it, etc., as recorded on file. It is found that the collection of additional land taxes in various provinces has long been clearly restricted by the Central Ministry of Finance. However, in recent years, each county has often raised local administrative expenses without complying with the standards set by the Ministry of Finance, each going its own way. The provincial finance departments arbitrarily impose additional taxes, or even the counties privately impose additional taxes, and the provincial departments have no record of it. Such unlimited collection, only aiming at the convenience of collecting additional taxes, levies local expenses specifically from the farmers and people who have land. The result is that it not only accelerates the collapse of the countryside but also affects the income of the regular tax, which is tantamount to suicide. It is urgent to quickly correct this. It is hoped that you will promptly and accurately list and submit for investigation to this headquarters all additional land taxes in each county and urban area under your province, and that you will thoroughly reduce the additional tax law and report it properly. Chiang Chung-cheng Seal." (2) "It is found that this headquarters convened a food conference on the 2nd and 3rd of this month, proposing to abolish harsh taxes and miscellaneous levies on rice. It was resolved that each province and city should thoroughly investigate the collection of rice taxes and levies and formulate effective reduction and exemption measures for implementation, etc., as recorded on file. It is found that our country is founded on agriculture. The common people work diligently throughout the year, and all they get is grain. Their clothing, food, and living all depend on it. However, it has recently been found that many rice-producing provinces often use the excuse that there are no funds for administrative expenses, and they actually collect taxes on rice. Even local groups below the county level create various pretexts to privately collect taxes on rice without reporting to the province for record. Layer upon layer of exploitation heavily burdens the farmers. Now that the bandit atmosphere has not subsided and the farmers are in deep distress, those in local authority should make it their top priority to relieve the suffering of the people. It is urgent to investigate the aforementioned resolution measures, supervise the officials under your jurisdiction to thoroughly investigate and list the various taxes and levies on rice collected in the province and city, and submit them to this headquarters for investigation, and effectively reduce and exempt these harsh taxes and miscellaneous levies. Chiang Chung-cheng."

Prohibit Hoarding and Obstructing Transportation 98

Chairman Chiang telegraphed the provinces to prohibit hoarding and obstructing transportation, roughly saying, "In the past, various places often used the excuse of disaster and insufficient food to hoard and obstruct transportation, hindering the circulation of food and creating a situation of confrontation between bountiful disasters and famine disasters. From now on, all such actions are strictly prohibited to allow for free buying and selling, connecting production and sales, and adjusting surpluses and shortages, thus avoiding stagnation."

Suppress Abuses in Grain Shops 99

Chairman Chiang also specially ordered the provincial and municipal governments to investigate and suppress the abuses in local grain shops, which monopolize and profit in the middle, disregarding the people's food and affecting the circulation of food, (1) stipulate their legitimate commissions, (2) cancel all extra miscellaneous expenses, and (3) supervise local chambers of commerce and grain trade associations to improve their organizations. (November 3)

In Areas Suppressing Bandits in Jiangxi, Divide the Garrison Area, 各Armies Firmly Defend Their Garrison Area, Thoroughly Blockade Bandit Areas 100

A telegram from Nanchang reports that Chairman Chiang recently announced ten items of improved bandit suppression tactics in "War and Youth," the third of which is to fix the garrison area of each unit for exclusive defense, that is, each army has its own jurisdiction, each division has its own jurisdiction, and so on to each brigade, regiment, and battalion, so that responsibility is clear, authority is centralized, and the organization is strict. It has now been implemented to delineate areas and, based on the terrain and distance adjacent to the bandit area and the distribution of bandit forces, assign the jurisdiction of each unit, designate the target for guerrilla warfare against the bandits and the scope of their guerrilla warfare and reconnaissance, so that the troops and targets within this scope are gradually advanced towards the bandit area in phases, by routes, and by areas, to fundamentally eliminate them. According to publicly released news, in addition to approving Zhao Guantao as the Garrison Commander of the Jiangxi-Zhejiang border and Zhou Hunyuan as the Garrison Commander of the Jiangxi-Fujian border, Chiang has also delineated Fuzhou, Nancheng, Qingjiang, Yongfeng, and other garrison areas, and appointed the army division commanders stationed in each area as the garrison commanders to maintain public order and facilitate the blockade, so as to prevent the Red bandits from escaping and causing trouble everywhere. (November 3)

Hunan Provincial Government's Strong Fundraising of Public Debt Causes Uproar, Bankers Sever Economic Ties with the Provincial Government, October Administrative Expenses Cannot Be Paid 101

A telegram from Changsha reports that the provincial government issued 5 million yuan of national salvation public debt, claiming it was for the purpose of resisting Japan and suppressing bandits. It was approved by the Central Government. The promotion method was to assign each of the 76 cities and counties in the province to raise tens of thousands or hundreds of thousands of yuan. Changsha City, as the capital of the province, was assigned to raise 1 million yuan. However, since its implementation, various counties and cities and Hunan fellow villagers in Beijing have risen up in opposition, or requested reductions. The provincial government knew that the people's strength could not overcome it, so it reduced it to 60%, actually raising 3 million yuan. Because there was no need to raise funds to resist Japan, it was changed to 2.5 million yuan for the Western Route Army's bandit suppression expenses, and 500,000 yuan for subsidies for recruiting labor to build roads, and it was set to subsidize 500 yuan per li. The original limit was to raise enough in three months, but now six months have passed. Statistics show that only 600,000 to 700,000 yuan has been raised in the entire province, and it was obtained through strict urging. For example, in Hengyang County, those who were imprisoned for failing to raise the required funds were overcrowded. In addition, appeals for exemptions and telegrams were endless. The 600,000 to 700,000 yuan that has been collected has come mostly from Changsha City. For example, the one-month rent of the entire city was levied, totaling about 200,000 to 300,000 yuan. Each collection staff member carried two soldiers and went door-to-door to urge payment. Those who did not comply were immediately arrested. Eight or nine out of ten have now been collected, and there is nothing more to change. In recent days, soldiers have been sent to various shops to urge the payment of public debt levied on operating capital. It is estimated that each money shop, gold shop, silk and cloth shop, and foreign goods shop has two or four soldiers stationed in the shop to demand payment. If the payment is not made one day, the soldiers will not be removed for one day. The home of Huang Bochang, chairman of the money industry association, also has four soldiers stationed and strictly pursuing payment. Huang was furious and resigned from the industry association. He also submitted a report to the government, explaining that this method not only hinders business but also causes panic. At the same time, the main figures of various industries in Changsha held a meeting and decided that unless the government withdraws the order to send troops to levy national salvation public debt, Changsha bankers would implement an economic boycott against the government, because the Director of Finance, Zhang Kailian, had to borrow 200,000 to 300,000 yuan from the city's bankers at the beginning of each month to pay the administrative expenses of various agencies. Today (the 4th) is the due date for the payment of administrative expenses for October, but it has not yet been paid, which is because the bankers have implemented an economic boycott against the government, causing the Finance Department to be unable to transfer funds. Zhang Kailian is very anxious and is currently asking Zuo Yizhai, chairman of the Changsha Chamber of Commerce, to mediate, hoping for a satisfactory solution. (November 4)

The Party Conflict in Hunan Province Rises Again, The Mutual Exclusion of the A and B Factions Intensifies, All Party Affairs Completely Stalled 102

A telegram from Changsha reports that cracks have appeared between the A and B factions of the Kuomintang Hunan Provincial Party Headquarters, resulting in the failure to convene the Fourth Provincial Congress of the Hunan Provincial Party Headquarters, which was approved by the Central Party Headquarters to be held on July 20, and party affairs have been stalled. The Central Party Headquarters sent Chen Lifu to Hunan to inspect and mediate, but without result. The Central Party Headquarters then stipulated four principles for resolving the Hunan Party conflict, ordering the A faction to reinstate the dismissed committee members, ordering the B faction committee member Liu Yuehou to express to the Central Party Headquarters the error of organizing the Road Association in the past and causing party conflicts in various counties, and the provincial party headquarters and the provincial government are responsible for preventing the provocation of party conflicts in Changsha's major and minor newspapers. After the above items can be strictly observed by both sides, the Central Party Headquarters will send personnel to participate in the preparation of the Fourth Provincial Congress. Three months have passed, and although the A and B factions superficially accept the resolution method set by the Central Government, they are still engaged in intrigue and secretly compete even more fiercely than before. In summary, among the seven executive committee members, the A faction members Wang Qi and Zhang Jiong are serving in the central government, remotely directing everything. Only Zhu Haohuai and Xie Zuyue are active in Hunan. The B faction is Tan Changkai, who has been transferred back to the central government. Because of the party conflict, the issue of succession has not been resolved for several months. He Jian and Huang Jiasheng have also requested leave for excuses and never go to the headquarters. Therefore, the Hunan Provincial Party Headquarters is only presided over by the A faction members Zhu and Xie, which is not enough to meet the legal quorum, and everything is still stalled. Moreover, the A faction has the central government as its backing and can command and order from top to bottom. The B faction is based on the party headquarters of various counties and cities and can launch everything from bottom to top by using the active forces of the Road Association in the party headquarters of various counties and cities. Recently, the party conflict in Hunan has reached the point of imminent clash. On October 27, the Changsha Municipal Party Headquarters, under the leadership of the B faction, held its 169th executive committee meeting and suddenly resolved to promote the opening of the Fourth Provincial Congress of Hunan Province, appointing Miao Kunce to petition the Central Party Headquarters and Huang Ji to petition the Provincial Party Headquarters. At the same time, telegrams were sent to the party headquarters of various counties and cities in Hunan.

The Whereabouts of Shi Dakai's Seal: Finally Falling into the Hands of a Sichuan Military Man; Central Government Orders Liu Xiang to Investigate, Confiscate, and Preserve 103

Chongqing Correspondence: Shi Dakai, the Wing King of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom, attacked and seized Sichuan but was defeated by Tang Junmen, the Qing army's admiral, who led his troops. Shi Dakai's seal was then obtained by Tang. The seal was made of wujin [dark gold], making it very valuable. Tang's grandson, Tang Wenyu, initially lived on Wenmiao Street in the South Gate of Chengdu. When Shi Zhaowu, the guard brigade commander of the 24th Army, was stationed in the provincial capital, he heard that the Tang family possessed Shi Dakai's seal. He then claimed that Shi Dakai was his grandfather and sent people to forcibly take the seal from Tang. This year, the Sichuan war broke out, and the 24th Army was defeated. Shi was captured by Li Qixiang's troops in Qionglai. After reporting to Liu Xiang, the pacification commissioner, Shi was executed by firing squad. Later, someone mentioned the matter of Shi Dakai's seal being hidden in Shi's home, and the matter was reported to the central party headquarters. The central party headquarters then telegraphed Liu Xiang, ordering him to confiscate the seal, send it to the headquarters for preservation, and then forward it to the Ancient Artifacts Exhibition Hall for display. Upon receiving the telegram, Liu Xiang ordered the Chengdu garrison to dispatch personnel to investigate and confiscate the seal. Recently, Liao Haitao, the commander of the garrison, replied to Liu Xiang, stating that Shi Dakai's seal had been lost. The original text stated, "Your subordinate

previously received Your Excellency's telegram in accordance with the Sichuan Provincial Party Headquarters' letter, regarding the seal of the late martyr Wing King Shi Dakai, which was transferred from Tang Baichuan to Shi Zhaowu's possession. We were ordered to investigate and confiscate it immediately, so that it could be transferred to the central party headquarters for preservation, etc. Upon receiving this, we immediately dispatched Lieutenant Colonel Zhou Jicheng and Councilor Hu Luban to investigate. According to the officers' report, Shi Zhaowu's family members stated that due to two street battles in the provincial capital, and Shi Zhaowu's subsequent death, they were displaced, and the whereabouts of Shi Dakai's seal were unknown. Just as we were about to report this, Shi Dihua submitted a statement claiming that her husband, Shi Zhaowu, had previously received a gift of Shi Dakai's seal from a friend, of which she was aware. Subsequently, due to two street battles in the provincial capital last year, all items in their residence on Gulou South Street and their relocated residence in the Wenzu Temple in the South Gate, including clothing, were lost, and the house was severely damaged. Shi Dakai's seal was also lost at the same time. After the war subsided, she immediately requested the 24th Army headquarters to record the loss for future reference. After the 24th Army withdrew this year, she had intended to request Your Excellency's headquarters to report to the Pacification Commissioner's office for record, but due to her husband's death, she was unable to manage household affairs and delayed until today to request Your Excellency's headquarters to record the loss for future reference," etc. According to this, we respectfully submit this document to Your Excellency's office for record." It is rumored that Shi Dakai's seal has not been lost but was obtained by Li Zongfang, the brigade commander of the Border Defense General Headquarters, who refuses to hand it over. Liao Haitao had no way to force him, so he fabricated a story to deceive the Pacification Commissioner's office to avoid further investigation. (November 5th)

Unanimously advocated. In recent days, party headquarters from various counties have responded with telegrams, and major and minor newspapers in Changsha, sympathetic to the Yi faction, have published articles supporting it, criticizing the Jia faction for delaying the Fourth Plenary Session of the Provincial Party Congress out of a reluctance to relinquish power. The Yi faction, with its influence in various counties and cities, aims to seize this opportunity to convene the Fourth Plenary Session of the Provincial Party Congress and achieve a decisive victory in the re-election. The Jia faction committee members convened a cadre meeting to discuss countermeasures, ultimately resolving on seven points: (1) Zhu Haohuai (Zhu is a committee member assigned by the central government to work in Hunan) was to secretly telegraph the central government, requesting changes to the electoral laws for the Hunan Provincial Fourth Plenary Session and postponing the session's convocation. (2) Large numbers of cadres were to be secretly dispatched to various counties to obstruct the dispatch of telegrams responding to and urging the convocation of the Hunan Provincial Fourth Plenary Session. (3) The faction was to secretly order its subordinates to create an atmosphere of manipulation of provincial party affairs through the "Road Association" and give it the name "Road Association Faction." (4) The faction was to use newspapers to fabricate various party affairs disputes to divert attention. (5) If telegrams urging the convocation of the Hunan Provincial Fourth Plenary Session from various counties and cities could not be prevented, they were to be secretly suppressed and not published. (6) Party affairs news was to be blocked, and newspaper reporters were to be denied entry to various departments. All internal staff were forbidden from concurrently working as newspaper reporters or communicating with newspaper reporters. A propaganda department cadre was to be assigned to exclusively release party affairs news to facilitate propaganda. (7) If necessary, the entire committee would resign again to prevent the convocation of the Fourth Plenary Session. Thus, the two factions have resorted to extreme measures, and the party conflict is escalating. (November 4th)

Hangzhou Coal Industry's Dispute with the Anti-Japanese Association 105

Hangzhou Coal Industry Association Urgent Telegram: To Shanghai Shenbao: Our association and the Hangzhou Anti-Japanese Association are embroiled in a dispute over Fushun coal powder. The Anti-Japanese Association has abused its authority by arresting staff members of various coal stores, causing unrest. Our association has submitted a petition to the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, the Zhejiang Provincial Government, and other agencies for review and protection. We are now forwarding the original petition via telegraph to your esteemed newspaper, requesting that you uphold justice. The petition is as follows: "Petition for the Hangzhou Anti-Japanese Association's Abuse of Authority and Illegal Detention of Merchants; Request for Legal Protection to Safeguard the Coal Industry. Since the September 18th Mukden Incident, Japanese aggression has incited national indignation. Our coal industry colleagues share the same enthusiasm for boycotting enemy goods. After being notified by the Anti-Japanese Association, fifteen members of the association, including Duntaisheng and Liu Dechang, immediately registered the remaining Fushun coal powder sold before September 18th, as well as the Kelazi coal from four companies including Mao Hengsheng Xiexing, with the association. In February of the 21st year [of the Republic, i.e., 1932], the Anti-Japanese Association, to facilitate public identification of Japanese goods, compiled and published a 'Comparison List of National and Japanese Goods' for reference by all sectors. This list was originally intended to guide merchants by the knowledgeable leaders of the Anti-Japanese Association and should have been printed only after thorough investigation and rigorous review. However, upon checking page 312 of the list, under the 'Coal' category, it was clearly stated that Fushun coal powder was a substitute for domestic goods. Only then did Duntaisheng and the other fourteen companies realize that their previous registration was a mistake. At that time, the January 28th Shanghai Incident was raging, transportation was disrupted, and the supply of coal in Hangzhou was becoming increasingly scarce, leading to a situation where demand exceeded supply. Therefore, they considered that Fushun coal powder, according to the Anti-Japanese Association's 'Comparison List of National and Japanese Goods,' was a substitute for domestic goods and should be sold to alleviate the market and prevent a fuel panic. Furthermore, Fushun coal powder has a high sulfur content and is prone to spontaneous combustion if stored for too long, posing a safety hazard. For example, Liu Dechang's coal has already turned into coal slag, which can still be verified. On March 20th, March 22nd, and July 13th of this year, six companies, including Duntaisheng, Liu Dechang, Taichang, Yinsheng, Renji, and Qiankang, received notices from the Anti-Japanese Association, stating that because they had opened the sealed goods without authorization, the Anti-Japanese Association demanded they confiscate the value of the merchandise from the six companies, including Duntaisheng and Liu Dechang, and imposed a fine of double the value of the merchandise etc. The merchants were astonished and immediately stated the facts in writing and protested twice. The Anti-Japanese Association ignored them. On October 6th, the Anti-Japanese Association, led by the guards of the association, illegally detained staff members of six companies, including Duntaisheng and Liu Dechang. Liu Dechang's registered Fushun coal powder had not even been sold, but the association indiscriminately detained and severely punished the staff of that company as well, and they have not been released to this day. The Anti-Japanese Association was established to boycott enemy goods. Its scope of punishment should be limited to goods smuggled in after September 18th. The Fushun coal powder of Duntaisheng, Liu Dechang, etc., was in stock before September 18th and had been identified by the Anti-Japanese Association as a substitute for domestic goods. Merchants selling it were not in the wrong and should not be punished. Even according to the directive of the Provincial Executive Committee (directive photograph attached), the Anti-Japanese Association originally listed it as a substitute for domestic goods, leading the merchants to sell the goods. Even if there was a mistake, the blame lies with the Anti-Japanese Association, not the merchants. The facts are clear and cannot be overturned. However, the Anti-Japanese Association dared to contradict itself, punish merchants, and openly go back on its word. This is truly a reversal of justice. Furthermore, the merchants voluntarily registered the goods, and the Anti-Japanese Association did not seal them beforehand. After the merchants sold the goods, they were accused of opening the seal without authorization, which is a completely fabricated charge. The merchants have protested repeatedly, but the Anti-Japanese Association has stubbornly ignored them, obscured the facts, and presented a statement to the Provincial Executive Committee to suppress them. The Provincial Executive Committee did not investigate the circumstances and hastily ordered that the case be handled according to precedent. This is either intentional bias or being deceived. The Anti-Japanese Association has become even more unscrupulous, abusing its power and ignoring the law, forcing merchants to pay fines and illegally detaining staff members. Their audacity is boundless, and there is no justice. Merchants who are engaged in honest business are being trampled upon, and they are truly aggrieved. If the Anti-Japanese Association continues to persecute them, it is feared that the members of the association will become indignant and automatically suspend business, causing a fuel panic in the market. Our association cannot be held responsible. We are expressing our grievances and earnestly appealing to Your Excellency to grant protection, to instruct the Hangzhou Anti-Japanese Association to release the illegally detained staff members first, to rescind the original decision, to exempt them from punishment, to uphold justice, and to relieve the hardships of merchants. We await your orders with utmost urgency. Respectfully submitted by the Hangzhou Coal Industry Association."

Qingpu: Neighboring Woman Kicked to Death, Four-Year Sentence 108

Wang Fei, a boatman from Wangchuan Bay, Zhangyan Town, Ninth District of this county, had an argument with his neighbor Wang Pan on the 29th of last month over a bamboo pole for drying clothes. The argument escalated into a physical fight, resulting in Wang Pan being kicked to death by Wang Fei. The town's security corps arrested the culprit Wang Fei and handed him over to the county government, requesting an autopsy. The next day, investigator Zhao Cheng and other officials and police officers went to the village for the autopsy. The autopsy confirmed that the deceased had been kicked in the small intestine, resulting in death. The county government recently brought the culprit Wang Fei to court for trial. Although Wang Fei refused to confess directly, the evidence was conclusive and difficult to deny. As a result, he was sentenced to four years of imprisonment.

Nanhui: Father and Son Bandits Executed by Firing Squad Simultaneously 109

Yang Hanchu and Yang Linsheng, father and son, natives of this area, were originally carpenters. They later joined bandits and engaged in kidnapping and robbery. On the night of October 2nd of last year, they colluded with escaped bandits Jiangbei Asan, Awu, Zhu Jinlin, and others to kidnap Zhu Xingen and Zhu Liangen, farmers from Caiyuan Township, Fourth District of the county, demanding a ransom of 2,000 yuan. In July of this year, the two bandits were arrested in Shanghai by the Fourth Detachment of the Provincial Water Police and brought back to the county for questioning. They confessed to the kidnapping and extortion without denial. They were sentenced to death in accordance with the law for punishing bandits, and the sentence was submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for approval. Yesterday afternoon, at approximately 3:00 PM, the two bandits, father and son, were brought from the prison. Investigator Hu informed them that they were to be executed by firing squad today and asked if they had any last words. At that time, the bandit Yang Hanchu repeatedly cried out for justice, while his son Linsheng angrily accused his father of ruining his young life. They were then verified, tied up, and taken to the execution ground outside the South Gate to be executed by firing squad.

Nantong 110

Criminals Apprehended in Tonghai Sent to the Capital for Interrogation

The governments of Nantong and Haimen counties have successively apprehended seventeen male and female criminals, including Gao Shaoqing, after separate investigations. They have now been sent to Nanjing by the Seventh District Commissioner's Office, escorted by police, to be interrogated by the Ministry of Constitutional Police.

County Magistrate Strictly Investigates Bandits, Communists, and Narcotics 111

Considering that the county borders the river and the sea, with convenient transportation, bandits and communists can easily infiltrate various ports, and narcotics can also be easily smuggled in, the county government issued an order to the Public Security Bureau and the police force on the 6th to pay attention to investigation and strictly prohibit bribery, cover-ups, and disturbances. All remote small ports along the river and the sea will be temporarily closed by the water police force for the winter.

Jiangyin: Public Security Bureau Chief Goes to Wuxi to Investigate Bribery Case at Branch Bureau 112

After Magistrate Ruan heard that Wu Bingjun, the chief of the Qingyang Public Security Second Branch Bureau, had discovered the secret manufacturing of red pills in the Huang Gonghe cocoon business in Xiao Qingyang, arrested the main culprit Chen Jinhe and others in Wuxi, and that there were rumors of bribery for their release, he ordered Liu Hanzhen, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, to go to Wuxi to investigate. There was no clue about the bribery situation, and he returned to Cheng yesterday morning (the 6th).

Qingjiang: Qingzhen Small Ferry Adds Regular Route 113

The Qingzhen Inland River Ferry Company, which already has several companies such as Tian Tai, Xie He, Zhen Tong, Fu Yun, and Zhaoshang, has been operating well in recent years. Now, Han Shaoshi and others have jointly invested in establishing another small ferry company, named Dada, which will also specialize in operating regular Qingzhen routes on the inland river. Preparations have been completed, and ticket sales for the regular route are scheduled to begin on the 10th of this month in Qingjiang.

Yangzhou: Anhui Refugees Passing Through Yangzhou 114

One hundred and twelve refugees from Anhui arrived outside the Yangzhou Customs at approximately 3:00 PM, went to the Fifth Precinct of the Public Security Bureau to present their passports, and requested that they be stamped to allow them to send representatives into the city to solicit food. The patrol officer in charge of the precinct contacted the Public Security Bureau by phone for instructions. He was instructed to prevent them from entering the city, but he was allowed to stamp their passports and escort them out of Yangzhou. The starving people left eastward on the morning of the 6th, passing through Xiannvzhen and heading towards Xiangxiahe in Taixian County.

Mingguang: Second and Third Districts Suffer Bandit Raids 115

In Renjiaying, the Third District of the county, more than a hundred local bandits suddenly arrived the night before, looting the entire village, kidnapping more than twenty men and women, and burning the houses to the ground. Subsequently, the local militia rescued and intercepted one hostage. In the Huang area of Yanwo in the Third District, a large group of local bandits surrounded the area last night (the 3rd), and the situation was extremely precarious. The county government and the stationed troops have dispatched teams to provide assistance.

Hefei: Liuan-Hefei Long-Distance Telephone Line Construction 116

Because the area between Liuan and Hefei has historically been a region where bandits are rampant and there is no long-distance telephone line, which is inconvenient for military affairs, the Construction Department has ordered the Hefei County Government to quickly prepare 1,775 poles (totaling 71 kilometers, 25 poles per kilometer), 1.5 zhang long and 5 inches in diameter, to be completed within one week, and to work with the Highway Bureau to erect the line. The county government has ordered the 17th, 8th, and 9th districts to prepare for its implementation.

Meres' Impressions of Chinese Railways: Railways Are a Valuable Asset, Should Be Preserved with Utmost Effort by the People 124

Xin Xin News Agency: Mr. Meres, chairman of the China-British

Banking Corporation,

recently visited major cities in North

and South China. At a banquet held on November 1st

by the Pan-Pacific Association and other members,

Mr. Meres shared his impressions of

this trip, which were published in the Continental Daily News.

The following is an excerpt concerning Chinese railways:

Mr. Meres felt that Chinese railways

were much more orderly than before, and that the service

personnel were not in the arrogant and

unruly state that he had observed when he left China in 1927.

In other aspects, Mr. Meres observed

many traces of natural damage, proving

that human intervention had been insufficient

in the past few years. He believed that

worn sleepers should be replaced and equipment

that needed replenishment should be replenished. He saw

many vehicles and locomotives idled on the tracks,

which he deeply regretted. He believed that

maximizing the use of locomotives and freight cars

is the secret to the prosperity of railways. The Chinese

engineers he met were doing their best

to compensate for this shortcoming. Railways are

a valuable asset that should be

preserved with the utmost effort by the people.

Mr. Meres observed the existing railways in this way,

and was very complimentary about the progress

China is making in building new railways.

He heard that China is making great

efforts to complete the Yuehan Railway.

The uncompleted section of the line

is currently estimated to be 275 miles.

He spoke with officials in Guangzhou,

who told him that once the line is connected,

rice from Hunan can be transported to Guangdong,

and salt from Guangdong can be transported to Hunan.

Mr. Meres urged the officials to pay

even more attention to the development

of coal mines along the line.

Cotton Yarn Exchange Incident: The Cotton Control Association's Attitude; The Suspension of Business at the Exchange Is Regrettable; But the Relief Work of the Control Association Cannot Be Delayed; Otherwise, How Can Millions of Workers Survive? 126

Xin Xin News Agency: After the establishment of the Cotton

Control Association, it received a letter

from the Ministry of Finance, stating that the Tax

Administration had submitted a request from the Chinese

Cotton Yarn Factory Association to maintain yarn prices,

and requesting that the association investigate the

reasons for the decline in yarn prices and

quickly discuss relief measures to safeguard the yarn

industry. After investigation, the biggest reason

for the decline in yarn prices since

spring was found to be that

Cotton Prices Are High, Yarn Prices Are Low 127

Cotton mills that were unable to sustain

themselves had to use inferior raw materials,

resulting in products that were not very

suitable for the market,

and speculators used this as a tool

to sell and dump yarn at the exchange,

resulting in increasing accumulation,

and yarn prices continued to decline.

Traders dared not absorb large quantities,

and domestic family weaving industries,

which relied on yarn shops for credit

to maintain their work,

mostly lost their jobs.

Therefore, the Cotton Control Association, after deliberation,

believed that, given the current autumn sales season,

in order to support the hand-weaving industry

and cotton mills, it was urgent

Methods for Relief: Moreover, the Chinese Merchants' Cotton Yarn Exchange, which was originally intended to balance the prices of cotton yarn, has now become a place for dumping goods. It should also be banned. The following measures have been decided upon: (1) The yarn stored in the exchange will be purchased by the Control Committee at market price, with a large portion transported to various places for sale. (2) The Control Committee will revise the exchange's standards and inspection regulations in conjunction with the exchange. (3) Starting from October, the Control Committee will dispatch experts to jointly inspect all delivered cotton yarn with the exchange. (4) The Control Committee will consult with the Chinese Cotton Mill Association to urge various mills to implement the resolutions passed at the association's general meeting on July 8th of this year (the resolution stated that from July 8th to the end of this year, the mills would no longer deliver yarn to the exchange), and also send letters to the Ministry of Industry and the exchange's supervisors for assistance. 128

[P Implementing this plan: Various measures are already being carried out separately. It is regrettable that the exchange had to suspend operations to implement item (4) under the order of the Ministry of Industry. Upon investigation, the yarn stored in the exchange has been increasing month by month from spring to autumn, providing speculators with opportunities to oversell at excessive quantities, which is an unavoidable fact. If this continues without relief measures, the nation's cotton mills and handloom weavers will eventually collapse. How will the millions of workers and villagers who depend on cotton for their livelihoods survive? Therefore, the Control Committee's current

Relief Efforts are both urgent and unchangeable facts. The brokers and speculators in the exchange should be able to express sympathy for the millions of farmers and workers who depend on cotton for their livelihoods. Moreover, this committee has already agreed on measures with the Chinese cotton mill industry: all goods sold by the mills to customers should be taken back by the mills themselves. The exchange's future regulations will be changed, transforming the real goods dumping market into a sound hedging mechanism. This is especially beneficial to the cotton industry and the exchange's brokers themselves. Therefore, it is hoped that all parties will contribute to its success. 129

Japanese Mail Ship "Heian Maru" Encountered Danger in the South Seas Due to Engine Trouble and Water Entering the Ship 135

The Guowen News Agency reported that the Japanese Mail Steamship Company's "Heian Maru" set sail from Shanghai a few days ago and was sailing in the South Seas when it encountered danger at 10:40 yesterday morning in the waters between the southeast of Hong Kong and the northern part of the Philippine Islands, at 119.30 degrees east longitude and 18.07 degrees north latitude. The incident occurred because the engines malfunctioned, the ship was unable to move, and a large amount of water entered the engine room, causing the ship to sink. The ship sent out a distress call by radio, and the coastal radio station immediately reported it to the Japanese Mail Steamship Company for rescue.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to Launch Water-Land Through Transport, Starting with Three Key Routes: Longhai, Jiaoji, and Pinghan 136

The 32 articles of the nationwide water-land through transport contract signed between the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Ministry of Railways have been finalized. The company is now planning to start with the Longhai Railway, as the goods from the northwest are most congested on this route, with large quantities of cotton and miscellaneous grains waiting to be transported. Due to the temporary wharf at Sunjiashan not being completed on the 15th, the sailing has been postponed for five days. Zhou Songnian, who was appointed by the Longhai Railway to Shanghai to handle water-land through transport, has arrived in Shanghai and is consulting with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to implement the through transport matters. The details are as follows:

Standing Committee Meeting Held Yesterday The Standing Committee of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company held a routine meeting at 4 PM yesterday. Attendees included Zhang Shouyong, Liu Hongsheng, 137

Ye Zhuotang, Sheng Pinchen, and Yang Zhixiong. The meeting began with General Manager Liu Hongsheng reporting on the progress of the water-land through transport with the Ministry of Railways' Through Transport Office. The contract agreed upon in Beijing was approved and will be submitted to the Board of Directors' routine meeting this Thursday for ratification. The progress will then be reported to the Ministry of Communications. The meeting adjourned at 6 PM.

Regular Service to Be Launched on the Longhai Railway 138

Water-land through transport on the Longhai Railway is scheduled to begin on the 20th. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has established a separate section to handle all operational matters related to through transport, appointing Zhou Fengtu as the director. The Longhai Railway Bureau attaches great importance to this matter and has also transferred eight staff members to Shanghai to be stationed at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to assist with the through transport of goods and the storage of goods at the docks and warehouses. The shipping rates for water-land through transport have been negotiated and set. The Railway Bureau has agreed to grant the workers at Dabu Port's request to employ half of the 3,000-plus workers to handle the loading and unloading at Sunjiashan wharf, in order to maintain the workers' livelihoods. Kang Zhenji has exclusively obtained the right to transport goods from Lianyungang. The Railway Bureau has also built a 5,000-ton capacity warehouse, free of charge, for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's ships to store goods. It is said that the first through transport ship on the 20th will still be operated by Tonghua.

Jiaoji Railway to Be Implemented Soon The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's second through transport route 139

under consideration is the Jiaoji route. Since the Northeast was seized, the goods from Jiaoji have been on the rise, especially miscellaneous grains and raw peanuts,

which are mostly transported to Shantou, Xiamen, and Guangdong. In the past eight months, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has earned more than 200,000 yuan on the Qingdao route. If through transport is implemented, the shipping industry will be even more developed. In preparation for the Jiaoji through transport, the company has leased Wuyang and Kunxing from Yuan'an Zhaoxing. The contract was signed yesterday for a monthly rent of 9,600 to 10,000 yuan. The ships will be designated to travel between Qingdao and Shantou, Xiamen, and Guangdong. However, during this process, the Jiaoji Railway Bureau and the Qingdao Port Authority have suddenly encountered a problem: the port authority refuses to accept the continuation fee for the transfer of goods to the dock, thereby making it impossible for the Jiaoji goods to be loaded onto the ships, which can invisibly hinder the through transport. It is said that this initiative was taken by a certain foreigner in the Jiaoji Railway. The Qingdao Municipal Government is currently negotiating with the Railway Bureau to resolve this issue satisfactorily.

Progress on the Pinghan Railway The third through transport route is the Pinghan Railway. The goods from this route are unloaded from Wuhan and loaded onto Yangtze River ships 140

for transport to various ports. The issues regarding the Pinghan Railway through transport are still under discussion. In addition to these three routes, the Jinghu, Wuchang, Huhangyong, and other routes are only embellishments. The quantity of goods on these routes is limited. Although the right to through transport also belongs to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the future transportation will still require overall planning, and the remaining goods may be allocated to privately owned shipping companies.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to Pay Lump-Sum Retirement Benefits to Foreign Crew Members, 248,000 Yuan for Eight Crew Members 142

In the past, due to a lack of specialized talent in navigation and engine operation, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company had to

hire foreign crew members for positions such as chief and second officers, and chief and second engineers. Their high salaries and excellent treatment were rare in the Chinese shipping industry. In addition to the high salaries, senior crew members were also provided with housing. During the privately owned period, even clothing was paid for by the company for washing. They had paid leave every six months, salary increases every year, travel expenses for returning home, and retirement benefits upon completion of their terms. At its peak, the company had more than 50 foreign employees, and their salaries accounted for a large portion of the company's expenses. Since becoming state-owned, the company has gradually employed domestic personnel in the navigation and engine departments, and has terminated the contracts of foreign employees whose terms have expired. Only a few remain. The total amount of retirement benefits and travel expenses paid to foreign employees by the company is staggering, and there have been disputes due to delayed payments. General Manager Liu Hongsheng believed that such complex disputes were inconvenient for both parties, so he proposed to take advantage of the company's reorganization and the addition of new ships to pay the retirement benefits of British crew members in a lump sum instead of delaying them in installments, in order to end the case early. The proposal has been approved by the Board of Directors. The amounts payable to each foreign employee are as follows:

Municipal Farmers Association Requests Protection of the Historic Site of the Xian Mian Temple Shanghai High School Sells Land, Municipal Land Bureau Investigates Property Rights, Reserves Land for Agricultural Exhibition Hall 143

The Shanghai Municipal Farmers Association has submitted a request to the Party and government agencies to stop the sale of the Xian Mian Temple by the Shanghai High School of Jiangsu Province (formerly Longmen Normal School) on Shangwen Road. The Municipal Land Bureau, upon receiving orders from the Municipal Government, immediately announced an investigation into the property rights of the temple. The Municipal Farmers Association has requested the Party to preserve the historic relics of past generations and designate them as an agricultural exhibition hall to commemorate the past. The details are as follows:

Investigation of Property Rights: Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau announced the investigation into the property rights of the Xian Mian Temple as follows: The Xian Mian Temple is located on the west side of Shanghai High School, and to the west of that is Yinggong Temple Road. According to Volume 12, Page 4 of the Shanghai County Continuation Records, there is a Huang Daopo Temple, and to the left of the temple is the Li Garden. After the garden was rebuilt into a academy, the temple was managed by the academy. The base covers 3 mu, 6 fen, 3 li, and 8 hao. In the 30th year of Guangxu (1904), the academy was rebuilt into a school, and the main gate, opera stage, and east and west viewing platforms of the temple were destroyed. A wall was built in front of the temple, with the inscription "Xian Mian Temple." Also, on Volume 12, Page 7, Yinggong Temple is located on the west side of Huang Daopo Temple, dedicated to the memory of Lang Heng, who was awarded the title of Grand Academician of the Inner Court and served as the Provincial Treasurer of Jiangsu and the Provincial Judge of Jiangsu, and who discussed the affairs of Su, Song, and Tai Dao. It was built in the 17th year of Guangxu (1891). The government authorities built temples, etc. Since the temples are recorded in the county records and are related to local ceremonies, they should be discussed by the Municipal Government, together with the Finance, Public Works, and Education Bureaus, in accordance with the request of Shanghai High School to issue certificates. Later, according to Zheng Tonghe, the principal of the school, an edict issued by Wu, the Civil Administrator of Shanghai in the first year of the Republic (1912), stated that the school could manage Ying Baoshi's private temple, which was built with private funds, according to the report submitted by Secretary-General Ying Dehong. The original property rights evidence submitted by Shanghai High School in this application for certificate renewal included two official management certificates issued by the former Shanghai County Government in March of the third year of the Republic (1914), one being No. 376, covering 2 mu, 8 fen, 6 li, and 2 hao, and the other being No. 377, covering 7 fen and 7 li 6 hao, totaling 3 mu, 6 fen, 3 li, and 8 hao. The户名 for both certificates was the Provincial Second Normal School, and the four boundaries were recorded as: east to the school, west to Yinggong Temple Road. The Xian Mian Temple and Yinggong Temple were originally located between Shanghai High School and Yinggong Temple Road. The property rights evidence seems to belong to the base of the two temples and were handled by the former Shanghai County Magistrate. However, the Xian Mian Temple is a historic relic related to the local area, and it is recorded in the county records. Currently, the Municipal Farmers Association, etc., have requested that the public property be preserved and designated as an agricultural exhibition hall. A request will be made to the Municipal Government for approval. 144

Another Request to Preserve Historic Relics: The Municipal Farmers Association submitted another request to the Municipal Party 145

Headquarters yesterday. The original text stated: "Submitted for the reason that Jiangsu Provincial Shanghai High School has arbitrarily sold the Xian Mian Temple. A request has been submitted to stop the sale. Please close the case and present the reasons again. We respectfully request your review. It is noted that Jiangsu Provincial Shanghai High School published an advertisement in May of this year to sell the school site on Shangwen Road, including the Xian Mian Temple base of 3 mu, 6 fen, 3 li, and 8 hao. The Association and the Zhabei District Farmers Association have successively submitted requests to your headquarters to stop the sale, preserve the historic relics, respect public property, and allocate the land to the Association to organize an agricultural exhibition hall. We subsequently received your headquarters' Instruction No. 563. As the case has been pending for a long time, the Municipal Government has not taken any action. It is rumored that Shanghai High School has arbitrarily sold the Xian Mian Temple's public property. In order to protect the agricultural community's historic relics, the Association has no choice but to restate the reasons. As stated in the county records, the base was only managed by the academy (the current Jiangsu Provincial Shanghai High School is the renamed academy), and the property rights do not belong to the academy. This is very clear. How did Shanghai High School obtain the property rights of the Xian Mian Temple? If they claim that possession is the same as ownership, that is tantamount to insider theft. Therefore, in terms of property rights, Shanghai High School also has no right to arbitrarily sell the Xian Mian Temple base. Moreover, the temple is related to local historic relics, is recorded in the county records, and has historical value. There is Xian Mian Temple Lane nearby, which is historically evident. How can it be buried? The sage Huang Daopo taught the people to spin and weave, and later generations built a temple to commemorate her. All farmers admire her. Now that the temple property is arbitrarily owned by the school, and the historic relics will be destroyed, all farmers in the city are extremely indignant. The Association, without fear of cost, reiterates the previous request. We respectfully request your headquarters to forward it to the Municipal Government to quickly stop Shanghai High School from selling the Xian Mian Temple base, and allocate it to the Association for safekeeping and to organize an agricultural exhibition hall, in order to preserve the historic relics and admire the sage. The presentation is urgent and we await your orders." Addressed to: Municipal Executive Committee.

Central Mint Machinery Not Damaged 146

The Central Mint has been in operation for half a year since it began minting. The new coins it has minted have long been circulating on the market. Recently, rumors have spread in the city that some of the factory's machinery has been damaged. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited the factory yesterday morning and learned that the water tower next to the factory's engine room suddenly broke down a few days ago, causing the water supply to be cut off. Therefore, the minting was temporarily suspended. Repairs are now underway and will be completed soon, and minting will resume as usual. The rumors of damaged machinery are not true.

Shanghai County River Dredging Conference 149

The Shanghai County Government, in accordance with provincial orders, is conscripting labor for river dredging. A five-year river dredging plan was previously drafted and approved by the County Political Conference and distributed to various districts for comments. The districts have successively replied to the county. A river dredging conference was convened yesterday, attended by the heads of the six districts under the county, as well as Wang Xuepeng, the head of the First Section of the County Government, Zhu Mingwu of the Technical Office, and local gentry Jiang Shijie, Kang Yongnian, etc. The conference was chaired by County Magistrate Pan Zhongjia, and the records were kept by Bi Huan. The discussion items were: (1) Should the county's five-year river dredging plan be established in general? Please discuss and decide. The resolution was: (A) The county's rivers will be dredged in five years, but the county has never had water conservancy funds. In addition to the earthwork, the costs of building dams, water drainage, surveying, etc., will be levied at five cents per mu from the first installment of land value tax each year, starting from the 23rd year, for a period of five years. This will be submitted to the Provincial Government for approval. (B) A portion of the levied mu tax should be allocated to the districts to subsidize the simultaneous dredging of branch rivers, in addition to being used to dredge the main rivers throughout the county. (C) The dredged mu tax should be kept in separate accounts by district. (D) The main rivers managed by each district should be surveyed on-site by personnel sent by the county before a decision is made after further consultation. (2) Should the county magistrate's proposal regarding dredging the Yingbin River be handled separately? Please decide. The resolution was: Reserved.

City Chamber of Commerce Continues to Request the Return of Fines for Hainan Sugar 152

Regarding the case of Hainan sugar being detained and fined, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday specially continued to request the Ministry of Finance and Customs Administration to promptly return the fine. The original telegram stated: "To the respected Ministry of Finance and Customs Administration in Nanjing: According to a joint telegram from the Ju Sheng and He Sheng sugar firms in Haikou, Hainan, regarding the case of fines for local sugar transported to Shanghai, the Inspector General of Customs has delayed resolving the matter. Yesterday, Zhi Cheng Xing, a merchant in Shanghai, acting as the fully authorized representative, went to the Inspector General of Customs to request instructions. We received a letter from the said firm stating that they did not meet the Inspector General, but were seen by Secretary Ding, who stated that he was fully aware of the situation, but that the matter could not be handled here and that they should await orders from the Customs Administration. It has been found that after the Hainan Customs fined the small merchants, various firms in this city transported sugar to Shanghai, and the Jianghai Customs verified that they were mixed with foreign sugar more than once. Light cases were fined, and serious cases were confiscated, with the Jianghai Customs verification being the standard. Even the Inspector General of Customs' telegram to the Haikou City Chamber of Commerce praised the Jianghai Customs for verifying the matter without error. Now that the small merchants' sugar has been verified by the Jianghai Customs as local sugar and has been proven in writing, the evidence is irrefutable. The Inspector General of Customs should order the return of the fine to avoid injustice to the merchants. However, the matter has been delayed for months, and recently, the excuse of not being able to handle it has been given. How can right and wrong be distinguished and fairness be shown? Because the Hainan Customs deliberately misrepresented the facts and intended to destroy local sugar, the small merchants dared not continue their business and were forced to temporarily suspend operations to await a resolution. The intangible losses are like years passing by. We respectfully request your council to maintain fairness and promptly request the Customs Administration to issue a clear order to the Inspector General of Customs, ordering the Qionghai Customs to comply and immediately return the fine paid by the small merchants in full to safeguard domestic products and ensure commercial stability. We would be extremely grateful." Based on this, it has been found that this case has been held up for months. Our chamber, after inspecting the Jianghai Customs re-verification, found that the certificate photo confirmed that it was local sugar. In July and August, we telegraphed your administration twice, requesting the Inspector General of Customs to return the fine to ensure fairness. Furthermore, in late October, Xing Juefei, the representative of the sugar merchants, presented a detailed account of the decline of Hainan local sugar and various relief measures to the Executive Yuan and the Ministries of Finance and Industry, requesting separate handling. We received your Eastern telegram in September, enclosing the photo and ordering the Inspector General of Customs to verify the matter. Now, according to the continued statement, the firm sent a representative to the Inspector General of Customs for face-to-face consultation, and the reply was that the authority does not rest with the Inspector General of Customs and that orders from your administration should be awaited for compliance. Therefore, this case does not involve the mixing of foreign sugar, which has been clearly proven. The fine should not be returned, causing the two firms to be suspended. Accordingly, we are telegraphing to request your administration to promptly instruct the Inspector General of Customs to return the aforementioned fine in full. We sincerely hope for your assistance. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce respectfully bows."

Jianghai Commercial Vessels Restricting the Hiring of Pilots: China Merchants Bureau Has Implemented It 153

For ships entering and leaving Jianghai waterways, some require pilots, while others do not, and the shipowners navigate themselves. Examples of the latter include Ningbo, Wenzhou, Fuzhou, Yantai, etc. Some ports, such as those in Japan and Dalian Bay, forcibly require pilots, and ships are not allowed to enter or leave without hiring one. Recently, some shipowners have deliberately hired pilots in areas where they are not needed, sharing the costs for personal gain. The China Merchants Bureau yesterday issued an order restricting the hiring of pilots, notifying all shipowners to comply. The original order is recorded below: Order No. 745 from the Shipping Department of the China Merchants Bureau: For the information of all concerned: It has been repeatedly ordered that ship captains of this bureau sailing along the Chinese coast are prohibited from hiring pilots. However, it has been found that some captains are outwardly compliant but inwardly disobedient, which is extremely inappropriate. Therefore, it is ordered again as follows: (1) Pilots may be hired at ports where pilotage is compulsory, such as Xiamen, Guangzhou (up to the Dashihe Fort), Tianjin, Haizhou, Dapu, Hongqi, Haiphong, Dalian, and all Japanese ports. (2) Qingdao is allowed to hire tugboats to dock and depart from the pier, but it is best not to hire them if possible. (3) In all other ports, except in special circumstances that should be requested temporarily, pilots shall not be hired for the ships. The ships all have wireless stations and can be used to request instructions from the port before arrival. (4) Newly appointed captains who are unfamiliar with the conditions in the ports of various ports are allowed to hire pilots, but not more than three times. (5) If it is found that pilots are deliberately hired or pilotage fees are shared, the pilotage fees paid will be deducted from the salary, and disciplinary action will be taken for violating the order. All are expected to comply. This order is dated November 6, 21st year, Director Zhao Yuntai, Deputy Director Zhou Houkun."

Supplemental Tax on Stored Shanghai Native Tobacco Leaves: Urgent Conclusion Awaited 154

The supplemental tax on stored Shanghai native tobacco leaves has been requested from the bureau by representatives of the Shanghai Tobacco Industry Association, and it has been approved to supplement the tax at one-fourth (that is, one yuan and four cents for every hundred market pounds). Merchants with stored native tobacco leaves should register with the Tobacco Industry Association, which will compile and submit them to the bureau. This has already been reported in the newspapers. If there are any stored native tobacco leaves that have not been registered, they can be quickly registered with the association. The deadline for completion is within one week. After the deadline, no more accommodation will be made, and it will be necessary to collect taxes according to the new special tax regulations, at four yuan, one dime, and five cents per hundred market pounds.

Yang Shousheng Kidnapping Case: Rickshaw Puller Dies from Severe Injuries 167

On the afternoon of the day before yesterday at 5:00 PM, several kidnappers went to the "Morimura Automobile Company," a Japanese-owned business located on Yalü Road in Hongkou, and hired a car with Concession license plate number 18066 and Chinese Area license plate number 4221.
