Gang Members Punished for Extortion 172

Han Yougen, a Ningbo native and employee of the Yongxing Fish Shop in the Hengtong Fish Market at No. 24 Xiaodongmenwai Street, French Concession, was forcibly extorted of 20 yuan on the afternoon of the 1st of this month by Liu Along (aka Mapizi Along), a local rogue, in collusion with his gang members Di Jundao, Zhao Hongbao, Shen Tianlu, etc. They forced him into Room 19 of the Yuedong Hotel at No. 23 Minguo Road, Dagu Road. When Han refused, they took out four sharp axes from under the bed to intimidate him. Han, having no other choice, paid them the 20 yuan he had on him and promised to pay the remaining 30 yuan the next day before they released him. Feeling resentful, he reported the incident to the police station, requesting an investigation. Han voluntarily offered to pay for a meal and did not extort him. Zhao Hongbao and Shen Tianlu testified that Liu Along had invited them to help with the matter. Afterwards, Han paid for them to have a late-night meal. While they were eating crab and drinking old wine in the room, the police arrived to arrest them. If they had extorted him, they would not have been so bold as to stay in the room and eat without running away. Furthermore, according to the patrol officer's report, no axes were found during the arrest. Finally, the police lawyer argued that the defendants used violence and coercion to force the victim to hand over his property, committing the crime stipulated in Article 318 of the Criminal Code, and requested that they be severely punished according to the law. 3,900 Yuan Fraud Case Involving Altered Checks Using Chemical Solution; Japanese National Guo Jiangpu and Li Jiaping Collaborate; American Lawyer Olmen Falls for the Scam; Case Cracked Recently After Five Months 173

On June 12th of this year, a Japanese national named Guo Jiangpu, using the alias Deng Tong, suddenly visited the office of American lawyer Olmen, claiming that a man named Li Jiaping owed him money and had repeatedly failed to repay it. He requested the lawyer to send a letter on his behalf to demand payment. After accepting the commission, Attorney Olmen sent a letter to Li (who was staying in Room 323 of the Zhongnan Hotel), urging him to settle the debt as soon as possible. Upon receiving the letter, Li immediately went to the attorney's office, stating that he was unable to repay the full amount and would first pay 100 yuan as interest. He then took out a check for 100 yuan from the Asia-East Bank and gave it to Attorney Olmen before leaving. Attorney Olmen then instructed someone to cash the check at the bank and temporarily deposit the cash at the Datong Bank, with which he had dealings. The next day, Guo arrived, and Attorney Olmen informed him of the progress. Guo stated that he would use the 100 yuan for other purposes and requested a check to withdraw the money. Guo obtained the check and then went to Li's residence. They had already succeeded in the initial stage of their fraudulent scheme and proceeded with the second step. Guo used a chemical solution to wipe away the number "100" on the check. After a night, the number disappeared completely without a trace. Li then altered the check, filling in the English number "3,900." Li had dealings with the Asia-East Bank, so he sent the altered check to the Asia-East Bank for collection from the Datong Bank. The Asia-East Bank did not suspect any alteration, and the Datong Bank did not detect any flaws, believing that the signature of "Olmen" was genuine. They immediately paid the full amount to the Asia-East Bank. At this time, Li Jiaping was unaware that the money had been cashed. Feeling guilty for his deceit, he dared not inquire rashly. He then devised a method of reconnaissance. He still had 20 yuan deposited at the Asia-East Bank, so he signed a check for 100 yuan and sent a tea servant from a certain hotel to cash it. If he received the full amount, it would mean that the money from the Datong Bank had been cashed. Otherwise, his fraudulent scheme would have been exposed. While he was hesitating, the servant returned, and he received the full amount. Overjoyed, he rushed to Guo to celebrate and, on the following day, drew a check for 3,700 yuan to withdraw all his remaining deposits from the Asia-East Bank. They divided the loot and spent it lavishly. When the Datong Bank discovered the fraud, they reported it to the police station, requesting an investigation. However, both Jiang and Li had already vanished without a trace. The incident occurred five months ago and remained unsolved. However, this pair of swindlers, colluding for ill gain, recently reappeared in Shanghai. Li had changed his name to Yang Rendan and was hiding in Room 526 of the Asia Hotel on Avenue Edward VII in order to find an opportunity to work. This was discovered by Zhao Bingkun, the Chinese detective chief of the General Patrol Office, and the Western detective Pratt, who launched a rigorous investigation. They arrested a suspect last Friday. Yesterday, the two swindlers went to the office of lawyer F. Crook in Yuanmingyuan Road No. 22, attempting to pull the same trick. They were then arrested one after another. Since Guo was of Japanese nationality, he was transferred to the Japanese consulate for interrogation. Yang Rendan was transferred to the First Special District Court yesterday morning for investigation. Yang is a Fujian native, only 26 years old. According to the police lawyer Ru Baoyi, the suspect had confessed to altering the check at the police station. He was charged under Article 224 of the Criminal Code, requesting a new date for the trial to be combined with the previously arrested suspect. Judge Feng briefly interrogated the defendant and ordered him to be detained and heard on Saturday.

Road Bureau's Attention: Baohuashan Longchang Temple; Special Order for Engineering Office to Inspect the Route from Longtan to Longchang Temple, Which is Related to Attracting Travelers on Both Routes 174

The Road Bureau previously considered Longchang Temple on Baohua Mountain as a scenic spot along the Nanjing-Shanghai Railway. They ordered the Engineering Office to study a route from Longtan Station to Longchang Temple. Engineer Yin Zhilu and personnel from the Traffic Office went to inspect the route and reported to the bureau. The route is related to attracting tourists on both routes. The following is an excerpt from their report. On November 25th, they walked from Longtan Station via Routes A, B, C, and D to Longchang Temple on Baohua Mountain. The distance from Route A to Route C is 11 li (approximately 5.5 kilometers), and the distance from Route C to Route D, where Longchang Temple is located, is 7 li (approximately 3.5 kilometers). The entire route is 18 li (approximately 9 kilometers). The width is about 4 to 12 feet. The road is paved with either bluestone or bricks, so it is very flat. Although it has been in disrepair for many years, walking is not difficult. This road is actually the main road from Longtan to Baohua Mountain. On the return trip, they took a four-person sedan chair from Longchang Temple, changing to Routes D, C, E, and A to reach the station, which is about 15 li (approximately 7.5 kilometers). Although this route is about 3 li (approximately 1.5 kilometers) shorter than the previous route, it is rugged and difficult to walk on. The section from Route C to Route E is very narrow, and there are not many brick-paved roads, but one can barely manage. However, at Route E, the winding path is difficult to navigate. There is a steep cliff for about a li (approximately 0.5 kilometers), making it difficult to cross even by sedan chair, and walking is also very dangerous. According to the sedan chair carriers, one can still travel on this road from Baohua to the station, but from the station to Baohua, one must take the Route A-B-C-D road. After investigation, there are many protruding rocks (limestone) along the way in Route E, which greatly hinders travelers. Removing them completely would cost no less than 400-500 yuan, but even if they are removed temporarily, the soil will be washed away by water in a few years, and the mountain valley will inevitably protrude again, which will be of no use. Even if the rocks are removed, the steepness of the slopes will make walking difficult. If the road is rerouted around the mountain to make it slightly flatter, it would cost no less than 2,000-3,000 yuan. In summary, since there is already a main road from Longtan to Baohua, there seems to be no need to find another route. Furthermore, the temple was named Longchang in the Ming Dynasty, renamed Huiju Temple in the Qing Dynasty, and now has reverted to its old name of Longchang Temple. It is located near the Baohua Mountain Ridge, winding along the side of the mountain for about 4 li (approximately 2 kilometers) to reach the temple gate. It is paved with bricks, quite wide, and lined with towering trees and flowing streams, making it a very secluded and beautiful place. The temple has about hundreds of rooms, which are neat and clean, with little noise. The surrounding bamboo forest is very elegant. There are about 100-200 resident monks. In spring and autumn, they hold ceremonies and set up altars, attracting many tourists. The temple's land produces about 5,000 dan (approximately 500,000 kilograms) of rice per year, and the mountain firewood can be sold for 1,000-2,000 yuan. The temple has 20 special rattan sedan chairs, carried by the temple workers, to pick up and drop off visitors. The fare from the temple to the station is 4,000 yuan, which is about 1.45 silver yuan. The Longtan Town has the Dingshui Temple, which is a lower temple of Longchang Temple. If the stationmaster notifies the lower temple one day in advance, the temple can send sedan chairs to the station to pick up visitors the next day. If visitors want to stay longer, they can also stay at the temple. Therefore, there is no inconvenience for visitors.

Foreign Merchants Exaggerated Price of Aristolochia Root; Profit by Six or Seven Times; Westerner Sends Letter to Newspaper Seeking Opinions from Chinese Merchants 176

Yesterday, we received a letter from a Westerner, Rizui, stating that Aristolochia root is a root of a shrub produced in the northern Kashmir region of India, on mountain slopes at altitudes of 4,000 to 5,000 feet. In recent years, China's demand has increased, with about 2,000 dan imported annually. However, because it is rare elsewhere, the Kashmir government has designated it as a national monopoly, collecting it from the people each year and selling it to the highest bidder. The purchase price is usually between 15 and 20 rupees per maund (approximately 82 pounds, equivalent to 0.615 dan in Chinese weight). In addition, the cost of transporting the goods from the Kashmir government warehouse to various ports in China is about 12 rupees per maund. Therefore, the cost of delivering to Chinese ports is no more than 32 rupees per maund, equivalent to no more than 65 yuan per dan in Chinese weight. Even if the Kashmir government and the purchasers each earn a profit of 100%, the selling price in Hong Kong and China should not exceed 130 yuan per dan. However, the price charged to Chinese merchants in the past ten years has often been between 350 and 480 yuan per dan, resulting in a profit of six or seven times. Based on China's annual import of 2,000 dan, the total cost of the goods is about 700,000 yuan. If the legal maximum value is used, it should only cost 260,000 yuan. China is paying an additional 500,000 yuan for this item each year. Only China wants to buy this item; other countries do not need it much. The reason why these merchants can obtain such extraordinary profits is that Chinese merchants do not know the cost. At a time when China is under construction, the financial resources of the people should be conserved as much as possible. If the chambers of commerce in various cities were to collect detailed information about this item and publish it from time to time, so that Chinese merchants can cooperate with each other to lower the price to a reasonable level, at least 500,000 yuan could be saved each year.

Yesterday, Judge Lu Renji opened the court for trial. The defendant retained lawyer Tian Heming for defense. Chen Qingyun stated that Shen Huiqun was a dancer whom he had met at a dance hall. Because she had no place to live, he let her stay at Jiande Apartment. She rented and lived there herself, and he had no relations with her. He was arrested for visiting and chatting, etc. Officer Zhu Zeming stated that on October 21, at 2 AM, after receiving a report from Shen Youtian, the precinct chief sent him to Room 29 of Jiande Apartment. He saw the woman sitting on the edge of the bed and the man leaning on the table. There was also a man and woman who said they were relatives of the plaintiff and were there to monitor. He then brought them back to the precinct. Shen Youtian stated that he was a collection officer stationed at Shenxin No. 9 Factory of the Ministry of Finance's Bureau of Unified Taxation. Shen Huiqun was born on May 25 of the Republic of China Year 3. She had previously studied and was not a dancer, but she liked to play. On October 12, she left with Mr. Wang, a former teacher, and did not return for many days. He found her at a friend's place surnamed Li, who eventually led him to Jiande Apartment. After questioning the tea house worker, he reported to the police and waited to apprehend them. (Question) Did your daughter claim at the prosecutor's office that she wanted three hundred yuan? (Answer) This was a proposal for reconciliation by relatives; I have no such intention. Shen Huiqun stated that she was twenty years old, born on May 25. Shen Youtian was her father, and she had a mother, four brothers, and one sister at home. Chen Qingyun met her at a farewell banquet for someone surnamed Li going to Nanyang. Afterward, he often came to visit. Because her father had a bad temper, she left home. Having no money, she went to the Bazilu Dance Research Association to borrow four or five yuan from Chen Qingyun, and he rented a room at Jiande Apartment. From this, a relationship developed. After three or four days, both parties discussed marriage and she wrote a letter to her parents to notify them and discuss it, but she did not know if they had received it. In August and September, she did work as a dancer at the Lafayette Dance Hall for three or four days, earning two or three yuan a day. However, she was not dedicated to this profession; she simply liked this pastime, so she quit later. She was very willing to marry Chen Qingyun, etc. The tea house worker, Li Xingsheng, also came to court to testify that the two had indeed been staying together. After much debate, the judge announced that the debate was over and a verdict would be delivered later. The defendant was remanded into custody.

Major Fire on Fuyou Road 187

—Six Houses Destroyed, Fire Burning for Two Hours—

Yesterday afternoon at 3:40 PM, a fire broke out on Fuyou Road in the city, burning for two hours and destroying six houses. Fortunately, no one was injured. Details are recorded below.

Fire Circumstances - Fuyou Road in the city, from Small World westward, is a concentration of foreign jade shops 188

Yesterday afternoon at 4 PM, the

Yichang Foreign Jade Shop at 405 Fuyou Road, owned by Lu Jinqing,

suddenly caught fire. Because foreign jade uses rosin as a raw material, the fire immediately broke through the roof and spread rapidly.

Six Houses Destroyed - After the fire broke out, the Zihua Street Fire Brigade was nearby and quickly arrived at the scene, but because the western section of Fuyou Road was narrow and the fire was intense, in addition to spreading to the Yongxingzhai Foreign Jade Shop at 403, owned by Zhou Yongde, and the Gong Yuanshun Cigarette Paper Shop at 409, it also affected the Fanyongji Paint Shop at 398 on the opposite side, the Daxin Wool Store at 396, and also spread to Wujianong, No. 2, Lanes 6 and 7, destroying a total of six houses. 189

Fire Starter Arrested - When the fire broke out, the relevant First Precinct of the Second Public Security District was very close. Precinct Chief Shen Zhenhua, upon hearing the alarm, immediately led his entire squad of police officers to the scene to suppress the fire, immediately arresting the fire starter Lu Jinqing and taking him to the precinct for questioning. Lu admitted to starting the fire and was immediately sent to the Public Security Bureau for review. 190

and half of them have already been reserved. Bird's-eye View of Rose Garden New Village | Robbery in Broad Daylight in Western Shanghai - Two Thieves Captured on the Spot - 198

Wang Jinxi, a local of Shanghai, opened the Sanxin Soda Company at 2018 Haig Road, Xujiahui, but recently the business has been slow, so it closed down the day before yesterday. Unexpectedly, yesterday morning at approximately 11:50 AM, Wang and others were settling accounts, preparing to pay off the soda company's debts, when four robbers speaking a Jiangbei accent and wearing blue cloth short coats suddenly arrived. They arrived in car number 18478 from Xiang Sheng Car Company. After getting out of the car on Rue Pere Robert, French Concession, they walked into Wang's shop. Two robbers held guns and robbed the place, while two robbers acted as lookouts outside. They robbed two hundred and eighteen yuan in silver dollars, twelve yuan in small bills, and sixty-five jiao in small change, fleeing eastward towards the wasteland of the French Concession. After seeing the robbers leave, Wang followed and shouted "Robbers!" and blew his police whistle frantically. Yang Zhongjin, a detective from the Second Precinct of the Sixth District, was passing by and, together with a guard from Yangjiaku No. 15, chased after them. At the same time, Hu Zongxi, a detective from the City Public Security Bureau residing at 2024, had just returned home from work. Upon hearing about the robbery, he also helped chase after them. The robbers fled to Rue Pere Robert, French Concession, intending to return in their original car, but the driver, Zhu Deshan, suspected them and locked the car, going elsewhere to buy cigarettes to observe the situation. The robbers, unable to escape, had no choice but to get out of the car and flee in all directions, opening fire on Detectives Yang and Hu to resist arrest. Yang and others also drew their guns and returned fire. The nearby French Concession police station on Rue Tong responded to the gunfire, dispatching a large number of detectives to surround the area. They chased them to the Pan Yunji Construction Company on Rue Canton, where they finally captured the bandits Yang Huaicheng from Jingjiang and Liu Zaishan from Qingjiang. The other two bandits escaped. They confiscated a handgun at the scene, and over twenty yuan in stolen money was found on their bodies. They were taken back to the police station and temporarily detained by Detective Yang in the Second Precinct of the Sixth District, pending the capture of the two remaining bandits, before proceeding with the interrogation.

Letter 207

To the Editor: In the November 6th issue of your newspaper, a piece of local news reported a rumor about paper merchants resisting goods, involving our society using enemy paper. After reading it, we were greatly surprised. The paper used by our society is all purchased from Xingji Paper Firm, Yuanhe Paper Firm, Yicheng Paper Firm, and Fufeng Paper Firm, and there are invoices to prove it. Moreover, each invoice clearly states the source of the goods, and we have never used enemy paper. Although our society is a merchant, we do not lag behind others in patriotism. Moreover, the current market price of newsprint in rolls is lower than that of enemy paper, so how could we abandon the cheap price and purchase the expensive enemy paper? This rumor is self-defeating. The matter concerns the reputation of merchants, so please correct it to clarify the facts and correct the rumors. This would be a virtue and convenience. Sincerely, The New Culture Bookstore of Shanghai, November 7th

Ministry of Education Explanation: Doubts Regarding Secondary School Law and Normal School Law 212

Regarding the request from the Ningxia Education Department to the Ministry of Education for interpretation of Article 8 of the Secondary School Law (Each secondary school shall have one principal; shall this appointment be directly commissioned by the Provincial Government, or shall the Provincial Government Committee pass it and instruct the Education Department to commission it?) and Article 10 of the Normal School Law (Having examined that the principals of provincial secondary normal schools have already been approved by the Provincial Government Committee, shall they be commissioned by the Provincial Government or by the Education Department?), the Ministry of Education has issued an explanation, stating roughly that the candidates for principals of provincial secondary schools should be proposed by the Education Department, and the letter of appointment shall be issued by the Provincial Government after the Provincial Government's decision. Article 10 of the Normal School Law and Article 11 of the Vocational School Law shall be handled in the same way.

Shanghai Education Association Requests Central Government to Unify Gengkuan (Boxer Indemnity) Management Methods; Central Government Responds by Referring to the Executive Yuan for Handling 215

The Shanghai Education Association previously stated that since the governments had not yet established unified management methods for the Gengkuan returned by various countries, and the real situation of income and expenditure was not clear to the outside world, and because there were rumors of using the Gengkuan to set up a Chinese International Library in Geneva, it had successively submitted requests to the Central Executive Committee and the Executive Yuan for review and instruction. President of Northeastern University Wang Zhuoran Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday to Wait to Meet Minister of Finance Kong to Discuss Funding 220

Northeastern University was originally located in Shenyang. After the September 18th Incident occurred and the border city fell, the university moved to Beiping. Zhang Xueliang continued to serve as president. This spring, Zhang resigned and went abroad, and Wang Zhuoran, the secretary-general of the university, took over as acting president and spared no effort in carrying out the university's affairs. During the Fifth National Games held in Beijing on the Double Tenth Festival, Wang led the heroic sons and daughters of the Northeast south to participate, which was highly praised by all parties. After the closing of the National Games, Wang immediately returned to Beiping with the Northeastern athletes. Wang took care of the university affairs slightly and then took a train south, arriving in Shanghai yesterday morning. According to reports, the university currently has more than 1,100 students, and plans to recruit new students next summer. The university's funding was previously set at 24,000 yuan per month by the Ministry of Education, but the Ministry of Finance only allocated 8,000 yuan due to the central government's financial difficulties, which made the university feel stretched. Now that the newly appointed Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi has taken office, I have come to Shanghai specifically to wait to meet him to discuss clearing the arrears in funding, and also to discuss the future plans of the university. Once things are settled, I will return to Beiping.

Inauguration of Xianzhou Cooperative Library, Founded by the Chinese Cooperative Society 221

When discussing the cooperative movement in our country, one must first mention Mr. Xue Xianzhou, a pioneer in cooperation. Mr. Xue returned to China from Europe around 1919 and immediately advocated the cooperative movement. To this day, most of the important figures leading the cooperative movement in the country are disciples of Xue. However, Xue unfortunately passed away in 1927. His spirit of advocating the cooperative movement has contributed to the party and the country and will be immortal. The Shanghai Chinese Cooperative Society, in order to commemorate the pioneer of cooperation and to encourage all members to work harder in the cooperative movement, specially founded a cooperative specialized library. Chen Guofu, Guo Renyuan, Zhang Dingzhi, and Wang Shiying were recommended as construction committee members, and it was decided to build the latest style library building on the society's base at Majia Alley, ZiWu Road, Nanjing. Construction began in May of this year and will be fully completed in mid-month. It is named the Xianzhou Mr. Memorial Cooperative Library, abbreviated as Xianzhou Cooperative Library. Recently, because the construction of the library is about to be completed, Wang Shiying, the director of preparation, has been actively preparing for internal equipment, library operations plans, and the solicitation or purchase of books. It is heard that the total construction cost of the library is in the range of 20,000 yuan, but a huge amount of funds is still needed for purchase and other regular expenses. A fundraising committee is being appointed to solicit donations separately. All parties believe that the society has made many contributions to advocating the Chinese cooperative movement over the years. The establishment of this library is not only something that should be done to commemorate the pioneers of cooperation, but also enough to emulate the Ireland Agricultural Organisation Society Cooperative Library, and will have a great relationship with the promotion of the Chinese cooperative movement in the future. It is heard that the fundraising for the library is progressing smoothly.

The Chinese Arts and Crafts Society Solicits Plans for National Revival; Deadline: December 20th of This Year; First Prize: Cash Reward of 200 Yuan 222

The Shanghai Chinese Arts and Crafts Society, in view of the urgent need for national revival, has launched a solicitation of plans for national revival to provide a reference for the Chinese people. The origins and solicitation rules are recorded as follows:

Origins of the Solicitation: Since September 18th, Difficulties Have Become More Urgent 223

The national situation is also dangerous. Knowledgeable people all believe that the way to save the country lies first in revitalizing the national spirit. Therefore, the call for national revival has become very loud. However, a concrete and complete plan has not yet been asked for. Therefore, the society launched a solicitation of contributions, hoping to provide a reference for the Chinese people, and prepared a small reward to thank the hard work of the great articles.

Rules for Soliciting Contributions: (1) No matter whether it is classical or vernacular Chinese, the limit is 224

20,000 words at most. (2) The handwriting must be clear and new-style punctuation must be added. (3) Submissions must be sent to the editorial department of the society at No. 45 Aimeiyu Road, French Concession, Shanghai, before December 20, 1933. (4) The author's name, occupation, and mailing address must be indicated on the manuscript. Those who wish to use a pseudonym when publishing in the future are welcome. (5) The submitted manuscripts will be reviewed and evaluated by experts hired by the society and published in the "Arts and Crafts" magazine. (6) One first prize winner will receive 200 yuan in cash, one second prize winner will receive 100 yuan, two third prize winners will receive 50 yuan each, and four fourth prize winners will receive 25 yuan each. (7) Whether the original manuscripts are accepted or not, they will not be returned.

Ms. Su Zengxiang Goes to Germany to Study 225

Ms. Su Zengxiang is from a prominent family in Gu Ying. She was intelligent and eager to learn since childhood. She graduated from the Municipal Wuben Girls' High School and then entered Tongde Medical College. She graduated in 1927 and opened the Dahua Hospital, which achieved remarkable results. She has extensive experience in obstetrics and pediatrics. She still regrets not having been taught by experts from Western universities. Now she has a lofty ambition to travel far away. She is scheduled to take the Italian mail ship Conte Verde on the 14th of this month to study in Germany. In addition to specializing in pediatrics and seeking further study, Ms. Su also plans to pay special attention to studying the latest European and American theories and methods for child hygiene and care, in preparation for promoting the improvement of our country's culture of raising children after returning home.

The Large-Scale Aurora University Museum; The Animal Section Has Already Been Opened 226

The Aurora University Museum in Lujiawan was completed in June of this year. It is large in scale and has a detailed collection, which is unique in Shanghai. The person in charge is Mr. Zheng Bier, a French national and director of entomology at the museum. It is divided into animal, plant, insect, antique, and library sections, as well as a medicine room and an office. The building is novel and the layout is well-organized. The animal section has already been opened in July, displaying various animals, such as tigers, bears, leopards, elephants, rhinoceroses, whales, eels, and hundreds of specimens, skeletons, and models of exotic birds and animals. The collection is extremely rich. The plant and insect sections have complete specimens, with approximately a thousand boxes, which are only for scholars to study and are not open to the public. If people from all walks of life need to study them, they can also apply to enter and browse. The antique section is currently being actively arranged. There are many kinds of items, such as Zhou tripods and Han tiles, ancient clothing and hats, carvings, jade ware, etc., totaling approximately a thousand pieces, which are priceless and rare. According to the person in charge of the museum, all the specimens and skeletons of various animals, plants, and insects in the museum were collected by the late Mr. Han, a French priest. He traveled to various provinces in China, as well as Nanyang, India, and Africa. They were previously displayed in the Xujiahui Museum, but the scale was small and not enough, so they were all moved here. As for the antiques, most of them were collected by a certain Westerner in Tushanwan over the years. After his death, they were all donated. Once the arrangement is completed, it can be officially opened in one or two months.

The Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Military Training Will Jointly Run Two Physical Education Schools; The Name and Methods Will Be Discussed Later 227

The National Sports Conference passed the proposal of the Ministry of Education to establish a Sports Committee. After the Ministry of Education organized the Sports Committee, it requested the Ministry of Education to propose the establishment of a National Physical Education School, which was passed by the 75th Executive Meeting and handed over to Minister He of the Ministry of Military Affairs and the Ministries of Education and Finance to jointly plan. Due to funding, location, and other reasons, it was not carried out. After the closing of the National Games, the Ministry of Education held the second Sports Committee meeting, and the old matter was brought up again, so it was decided to propose it to the Executive Yuan meeting again in order to realize this matter. Recently, the Ministry of Military Training intends to run a National Military Sports School, which has the same purpose as the National Physical Education School that the Sports Committee of the Ministry of Education intends to run. It is heard that the Sports Committee will send representatives to the Ministry of Military Training to discuss the principles of cooperation in the near future, according to the resolution. The so-called Military Sports School and the National Physical Education School may be merged into one in the future. As for what it will be named and the detailed methods, it will be necessary to wait until the Sports Committee and the Ministry of Military Training have made contact before they can gradually plan.

Chinese Race Walking Association: Open Race Walking for Men and Women; 197 Participants; Notice on Competition Guidance Released 229

Since the preparation for the 3rd Chinese Open Men's 13-Mile and the 1st Women's 1-Mile Race Walking Competition of the Chinese Race Walking Association, the results have been very good. There has been a enthusiastic response to the registration. The registration deadline was 9:00 p.m. last night. There were six groups for men, including Chenguang Group A and B, Huxi Group A and B, and Sanduo Group A and B, with 140 individuals. There were 57 women. In total, there were 197 men and women. After repeated practice, the results are quite good. When the competition comes, it will inevitably be fierce. In order to facilitate the competition of the athletes, take care along the way, and arrange clothes, the association requires each person to invite a guide. They must attend together at the time. As for the knowledge and various rules that competitors and guides must know during this competition, they are extremely important, and are recorded separately as follows:

Competitor's Notice 230

(1) Competitors must proceed on the prescribed avenue and are not allowed to step onto the sidewalk. (2) When a competitor overtakes a competitor in front, they must maintain a distance of three steps to the left or right before proceeding.

(3) If a competitor has other reasons during the competition, they may be allowed to leave the designated road, but they must return to the original place before proceeding.

(4) Competitors must keep their chest straight, swing their arms freely, and use their heels and toes when striding, but the heel of the front foot must not touch the ground until the toe of the rear foot is lifted, and the knee must be straight when the front foot touches the ground (it must be straight when the rear foot is lifted).

(5) If a race walker violates the above rules, the referee on the way will warn them and punish them with one turn; on the third time, their competition qualification will be cancelled.

Guide's Notice 231

(1) Start introducing and exiting at the prescribed location.

(2) May ride a bicycle or walk.

(3) Guides must not follow others in the race walker they are assigned.

(4) Apart from providing food and drink to the race walker, they are not allowed to touch the competitor.

(5) When a race walker behind overtakes, the guide in front must not deliberately obstruct.

(6) If the above rules are violated, the referee on the way will also warn them or cancel their qualification as a guide.

Spring and Autumn

War 244

— Hua Ling

According to the predictions of the foreign Liu Bowen, the Second World War will break out in the Far East between 1935 and 1936, and China's coastal areas will be affected by the war. As a result, some neurotic people are restless and planning to go to the Pamir Plateau to take refuge. Whether this plan is what is called containing a hidden beast meaning, deliberately pretending to be such a panic, I am not very clear, but according to my experience in several civil wars and foreign wars, I feel that war is not so terrible.

In war, there is naturally the danger of being killed by bombs dropped from airplanes, being killed by stray bullets, being captured and killed by enemy troops as plainclothes teams, and being beaten to death by the people as traitors, but if you dig a cellar in advance, hide good food, and wait to see sandbags and barbed wire, you can drill into the cellar to hide, without fail. If you are blessed by the Tai Bai star and protected by the Zi Wei star, then you will not die, and it doesn't matter if you just hear about it outside. You see, in the European war, except for those who were destined to die, those who were not destined to die are still living well, eating bread and drinking wine.

Those who dig cellars are naturally people who value their lives as much as Mount Tai. Life is a hundred years, and one cannot escape death in the end, so those who think more openly simply sit down with four people and play the thirteenth chapter of Zuo Zhuan, because the sound of the tiles can cover up the sound of guns and cannons on the front line, eliminating the terror of war.

People with vision should hurry to open a hotel, or rent several pavilions and three-story railings, and they will surely make a fortune. On a smaller scale, go and contract a large number of extra editions, or print in advance some telegrams of the enemy's generals being killed on the same day, and when the firecrackers go off, you will surely make a big profit. Tuibeitu and Shaobing Ge can also be sold. To put it more unambitiously, becoming a petty traitor is not a bad business.

Those who are not destined to die don't need to rush, they won't be killed. Those who are destined to die don't need to rush either, eating some Tian Hua Fen can also choke you to death. War is not as terrible as we imagine, so there is no need to go to the Pamir Plateau to take refuge, let alone make a long journey.

King 245

— Qian Jian

The word "King," whether heard or seen, will evoke twelve points of envy and admiration. Because the title of "King" must be unique in a line to be worthy of the name. In fact, the title of "King" is indeed very rare and uncommon in the world. Therefore, the two words "King" have become a supreme honorific.

"King" has a wide market abroad, so the title of "King" is also obtained very often. For example, in the automotive field, there is an Automobile "King." In the kerosene field, there is a Kerosene "King." In the steel industry, there is a Steel "King," and there are other such "Kings," popping up everywhere, making it too numerous to list.

However, "King" has a special market in China. Although there is no Automobile "King," no Kerosene "King," and no Steel "King"; peanuts have a Peanut "King," sunflower seeds have a Sunflower Seed "King," and beef has a Beef "King." "King" has been made so diverse that it is truly impossible to sort out.

You call yourself "King," and I call myself "King," to the point that the two words "King" themselves are at a loss and cannot agree. Therefore, "King" had to seriously consider, thinking left and right: foreign cars, kerosene, and steel want to add the title of "King" because they are Kings and are called "King." Adding "King" to them is a great honor. Not to mention that each owner calling themselves "King" will thank me, but I myself have supreme glory. Not to mention that each owner has face, even my two words "King" have face. At the same time, Chinese peanuts, sunflower seeds, and beef also want to add "King," which is truly absurd. The very essence of "King" cannot help but be filled with sorrow. Many thoughts welled up in the heart of the two words "King." It thought: the "King" of Chinese Peanut "King," Sunflower Seed "King," and Beef "King" will be confused with the "King" of Automobile "King," Kerosene "King," and Steel "King." Isn't this too insulting to "King"!

When "King" thought, it felt twelve points of indignation; but in fact, it could not forcibly argue, and could only let it pass roughly.

In the end, the very essence of the two words "King" revealed a burst of satirical sneer.

Talking About a Few Things About Women 246

— Xiao Gong

I remember when I was studying in Beiping a few years ago, there was a beautiful female classmate who often showed off many letters from men asking for her love in front of her friends, thinking it was the supreme glory, and at that time, none of her friends did not envy her. Also, once I went to a friend's house, and it happened that his wife was playing cards with three other ladies. At that time, another richly dressed lady walked in, and everyone stood up to greet her. One of the ladies, perhaps paying attention to the cards in front of her, had not yet risen to her feet, and this richly dressed lady immediately ran in front of her and asked her:

"Where does your old man work?"

"In XX Foreign Company."

The lady immediately turned her face and loudly rebuked her:

"Just because you're an employee of a foreign company, you're so impolite? Our old man is the manager of XX Bank!"

This is so glorious! Our old man is a bank manager, but thinking about it the other way around, this is a woman's greatest shame.

In fact, when this richly dressed lady said these words, she had not anticipated her own position. She thought that she was the absolute possession of her husband. "To beat a dog, one must look at the master's face," so she dared to boldly scold the impolite lady, that she should not be so impolite to her, because my husband… the master… is a bank manager.

From the above two small things, we can think of the psychology of ordinary women now, still not shaking off the bad habit of relying on men, even willingly admitting that they are not as good as men! This is truly a very shameful thing!

Here, I think of a story of Wu Zetian, the only female emperor in our country:

Emperor Taizong of Tang once obtained a strong, fat horse,

but no one could control it. Wu Zhao then went up and said to Emperor Taizong, "I can control this horse. But there are three things: an iron whip, an iron mace, and a dagger. If it does not submit to the whip, then mace it; if it does not submit to the mace, then cut its throat!"

What courage, what power! We need not elaborate on Wu Zhao's great contributions to women's liberation later. Just this one thing is enough to tell us that there was such a woman in ancient China. Her strong and resolute personality was no less than that of a man. But how today's women feel about Wu Zetian is unknown.

Autumn Painting 247

— Fu Yiye

If we recognize spring as the season of flowers, then autumn is the season of leaves. There is nothing in a year as magnificent as the flowers of spring, nor is there anything as rich and brilliant as the leaves of autumn. Autumn is the most beautiful season in nature, and it is also the most suitable time for color painting. Autumn, is it a painting autumn?

On the vast river, the sky is blue, and large patches of white clouds are flying. Withered grass and reed flowers are gathering a rustling autumn feeling in the west wind. In the distance, a few sails are returning with the afterglow of the setting sun, evoking the reverie of distant travelers. This is the autumn painting on the river.

On the undulating peaks and mountains, there are forests intertwined half sparsely and half densely. Here, there are towering strange rocks, ancient trees with the power of dragons, complex and mottled red leaves, colorful autumn mountains. In the winding paths and cliffs, two or three woodcutters are carrying firewood, faintly climbing the mountain, arousing feelings of pastoral interest. This is the autumn painting in the mountains. But, the scenery on the river is far less beautiful than the scenery in the mountains, that is because the colors in the mountains are actually richer than those on the river. These colors are dyed by countless leaves of varying depths and shades. A single leaf is like a rainbow in the sky, a beautiful feather on a phoenix, a fine powder on a butterfly's wing. It is nature that weaves a huge and beautiful autumn painting.

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 248

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 18: Silently Passing Tea with Sorrow to Comfort Her Husband, Hastily Leaving the Border with a Forced Smile to Say Goodbye to Her Family

Jiang nodded silently, neither agreeing nor disagreeing, and let them go. She was thinking to herself, once a girl has a husband's family, her heart will naturally follow her husband. Look at her, even though she is extremely sad, she still wants to put on a pretty face in front of her husband, patting on powder several times, before leaving. This shows that a woman always seeks her husband's happiness. Without a husband, everything is gone. She stayed alone in the house, thinking dully. She didn't know how much time had passed, only to see the sunlight on the wall in the courtyard had slanted to the eaves, and was tinged with a golden yellow. This undoubtedly meant that it was almost evening. Only then did she wake up. This couple used to not care about going out, how is it that now that they have gone out, they don't know when to come back. She couldn't stand being alone, so she ran to the back courtyard to talk to Zhao Weng for a while. Zhao Weng also felt the same as his son, only feeling sorry for the other person, and tried his best to comfort her with words. After a while, she heard the sound of leather shoes in the front courtyard. Jiang knew that Ziqiang and Guizhi had returned, so she immediately ran to the outer courtyard. Zhao Ziqiang walked quickly and had already reached the door of the back courtyard. Guizhi, however, stood in the outer courtyard with her head half-lowered. When she left, her face was snow-white, but now, on her yellowish face, hung streaks of dry tear marks. Her eyes were red and unusually swollen. Just looking at her lowered eyelashes, in that silent moment, she must have gone through an extremely sad event. But the bitter water in her daughter's heart, she knew herself, and if she tried to gloss over it, she might be trying to hide it from her mother. If she asked her, it would only provoke her complaints. Therefore, Jiang did not stare at her face, and went into the house by herself. (234)

Wandering in the Arts

Discussing Comics 249

— Huang Shiying

Comics, it can be said, are very popular lately. They have been published sporadically in magazines and newspapers, especially as embellishments in daily newspaper supplements. Special issues and special editions seem to be a very fashionable attire, and everyone is vying to imitate them. On the surface, it seems that comics have reached a prosperous period, but is it really prosperous? We might as well discuss it from the origin of comics and the recent quality of content.

I. A Retrospective of Comics in China

In this Eastern country, which absorbs Western civilization as much as possible, following Western civilization is considered an honor everywhere. Comics are also a kind of Eastern expansion of European style. Five years ago, cartoonists in Shanghai jointly published "Shanghai Comics," establishing a foundation for comics in the dull Chinese society. It was also a preliminary understanding of comics for people in society. Unfortunately, this pictorial died young! It could not form a lasting gathering with its newly acquainted friends, but its seeds had already been sown. The impression it gave to readers surpassed a sweet and delicious fresh fruit, thus arousing the interest of comrades and engaging in practice. This is the first stage of comics in China. Since then, these comrades who have become interested in comics have continued to publish "China Comics," "Weekly Comics," "Linglong Comics," and other publications, although they also ceased publication soon. However, they have aroused the attention of the press. Thus, from independent publications to newspaper comic supplements, it can be said that comics have entered the second stage. Comics have become widespread through newspapers, thus gaining the interest of a wide range of readers. The future of comics in China has unfolded a bright path!

II. The Distorted State of Today

Comics are an art, using the power of this art to negatively criticize life and positively create life. Therefore, cartoonists should have a calm mind to observe all the secrets of society, and in light and flexible painting techniques, make people see their ridiculous and pitiful true faces. Therefore, they must grasp the spirit of the times to promote the strength of the nation! They occupy the same important position as writers and sculptors, and can achieve greater results. But can our so-called comics now fulfill this mission?

In China, where everything is backward, comics cannot escape their backward fate! Perhaps it is excusable, but we are always discovering this kind of superficial and simply ridiculous things in the newspapers, which is a bit disappointing! I think, more practice and more promotion are indeed good, but why publish so much? To know that just drawing a picture randomly and calling it promoting comics will only make things worse. Not only will it not contribute to comics, but it will also lose the true meaning of comics. What a painful thing this is!

Newspaper editors, of course, are enthusiastic about promoting comics, so they indiscriminately gather these people and place this responsibility on them. They have such opportunities, but they do not work hard. If their own strength is insufficient, they copy and steal. As a result, copied works that are half as good as the original fill the publications. This is a tragic phenomenon in the distorted development of comics in our country recently!

III. Hopes for the Future

Now comics are indeed very popular. If we can put in a lot of effort in terms of thought and skill, then the hope for the future is really great. If we are always childish in our thinking and have not been trained in skills at all, and publish randomly in newspapers, this will cause readers to have a bad impression of comics, and even dislike them! Therefore, we must carefully cultivate this newly growing seedling, and we should rectify the pace of comics, from superficial to profound, from simple to complex, from animal desires to truth, from individual to society. We must earnestly polish and cultivate our thoughts and techniques, correct this distorted art, and achieve good results, so as not to waste the efforts of all comrades.

Free Talk

On Using Vernacular Chinese in Official Documents 250

— Yu Dafu

Recently, I have been hearing many contradictory news at the same time. One just said that those in charge of education are encouraging the reading of scriptures again, so "Huang Qing Jing Jie" and "Thirteen Classics with Annotations and Commentaries" have become popular again recently; another said that official documents should also use vernacular Chinese, or at least use some new-style punctuation and symbols. A few days ago, a friend who works in an office came to me to discuss the writing of vernacular Chinese and the use of punctuation marks. I asked him how classical Chinese was done. He said: "The method of classical Chinese is very easy. For example, for official documents, just teach a few '...'etc., and then copy the text. No matter how complicated the case file is, it will be clear at a glance." His words seemed to regret the beautiful official document format that was about to be abolished. I told him that there was no need to be pessimistic, this official document format could not be abolished no matter what. Because China has always been a country that reveres the past, even in the Qin Dynasty, Confucian scholars were required to take officials as teachers?

"But now the situation is different!" he said worriedly.

Because I had no way to dispel his worries, I had no choice but to think of Stendhal and say: "Please rest assured, this great French writer was still imitating Napoleon's legal terms and sentence structures when he wrote articles!"

The advocacy of vernacular Chinese has had more than ten years of history so far, and as a result, it has only occupied a few punctuation marks and symbols in six-character notices and official documents such as "...etc.", which has caused a large group of people to be furious and indignant. I really don't know in which year the entire feudal system will be swept away?

On the "Opium War" 251

— Sun Bo

After reading "Tokyo View of the Roar" published in "Free Talk" on October 17, Mr. Jusheng pointed out "A Mistake by Mr. Gaoming" in "Free Talk" on October 27, meaning: "The Opium War" was written by Tomoyoshi Murayama, while Mr. Gaoming mistakenly thought it was written by Kan Eguchi. But in "Free Talk" on November 1, Mr. Gaoming again "protested," saying that "as far as I know, the Opium War was indeed originally written by Mr. Kan Eguchi." This has made us "uninformed" readers a bit "mystified." 丨丨 Who exactly is "The Opium War" the work of? Murayama? Or Eguchi?

"As far as I know," in Japan, there are two dramas with the Opium War as the theme: one is "The Opium War" by Osamu Ema, and the other is "The First European Flag" by Tomoyoshi Murayama. And Murayama's work is actually very related to Ema's work. According to Murayama's preface to the drama collection "The First European Flag," at first, because he was not satisfied with Ema's work, when the play was staged at the Tsukiji Theater (August 1929, directed and designed by Murayama), he obtained the author's consent and made major revisions, resulting in a collaboration between the two people; but, since that performance, he was even more dissatisfied with that kind of confusion, so he simply rewrote it completely. As a result, "The First European Flag" is actually completely different from "The Opium War."

Based on the above facts, we can easily understand:

First, the original author of "The Opium War" should be Osamu Ema, not Kan Eguchi ("As far as I know": Mr. Eguchi's works are mostly novels and fairy tales, with very few dramas). Mr. Gaoming obviously mistook Osamu Ema for Kan Eguchi. Second, Mr. Jusheng pointed out that "The Opium War" was written by Mr. Murayama, which is naturally not wrong, because "The First European Flag" is also known as "The Opium War." However, I feel that in this kind of place, after pointing this out, it should also be explained that Mr. Osamu Ema also wrote the play "The Opium War." Because judging from the time (four or five years ago), location (Hongō Theater), and performing troupe (Tsukiji Troupe) of Mr. Gaoming's play, the "Opium War" he saw was obviously a script co-authored by Osamu Ema and Tomoyoshi Murayama: and in fact, Murayama at that time was only a reviser, and perhaps the script still used the name of the original author Osamu Ema (a name with one character the same as the name of Kan Eguchi) during that performance.

The above is the fact "as far as I know." I dare not flaunt "high intelligence," but just record what I know.

On the Street 252

— After Turning Peng

The weather is getting colder, and the great frost of November is brewing, and soon it will begin to fall·······

On a gloomy day, a strong wind rolled up the yellow plane tree leaves on the street. At the corner of a road, the wind swirled, and the fallen leaves swirled. On the side street of Cement, a dirty beggar woman was sitting with her knees bent against the wall. Her feet were wrapped very small. She was wearing a man's tattered jacket, and her breasts were like deflated rubber bags, hanging empty······ A baby less than one year old sucked on the nipple, and his small hands tightly held the mother's breast, as if to squeeze out as much milk as possible. Another child of seven or eight years old, naked in the upper body, lay on his mother's knee, silent, like a wounded, dying little animal. A gust of cold wind blew, and he shrank his body and convulsed······

"Have mercy, madam, grandma······ the child is freezing to death······ starving to death······"

The mother begged the passers-by with a crying voice, putting her hands together and touching her head on the ground.

The beggar woman relied on this half-naked child to beg, letting the child freeze in this cold, windy weather, to gain some sympathy and alms in front of people.

Groups of people walked past, not even glancing at her······ "Have mercy······"

The mother's throat was dry and hoarse. Her throat was on fire, and her stomach was on fire.

The sky gradually darkened, and the street lights lit up, like laughing, satirical eyes, the city became more beautiful.

The child raised his drooping, heavy head and stared at his mother, looking at her face.

"Mom, how many copper coins do you have?"

The mother fumbled in her pocket; "One, two, three·······"

"Not enough to drink two bowls of porridge······ only to drink water, only······"

The child lowered his head again, his skin frozen and swollen purple.

"Let's go back丨"

The mother said; holding one child in one hand and leading one child in the other.

At night, the weather was even colder. The great frost of November was brewing, perhaps it would begin to fall tonight·······

Reading Notes 253

— Xiaoxue

A few months ago, in the magazine "Unnamed Literary Monthly," I read "Harvest" by Ye Zijun. At that time, I wanted to write a few words, but because the magazine was borrowed by someone soon after, it was put on hold. Yesterday, I bought a newly published "Literature," and in it, I saw the sequel to "Harvest" by Ye Zijun, "Fire." Eager to know the new developments of this writer in a few months, I read it first. Now, according to the annotations at the end of the article, let's connect the two articles together and express some opinions.

Regarding "Harvest," because the magazine is still with a friend, I can only speak based on the outline I wrote down at the time. This novel, at that time, could be said to be until now, deeply aroused my attention, which can be said to be the rich rural life experience. Among the several novels depicting the disaster of a good harvest produced in 1933, this article is probably the most substantial in content. The author is really familiar with rural life. Although the technique is not very pure, under the author's pen, there is endless truth of life crowded there, which everyone will feel. To describe farmers, the author must truly understand rural life in order to have good success; only in this way can we overcome the tendency of good content being empty, specializing in using skills to make up the number of words, and showing off. Because of this, I think the future of this writer is very broad. Secondly, what makes me satisfied with this novel is the description of the joyful atmosphere about the harvest before the harvest. Mr. Ye Shengtao's "More Harvested Three to Five Dou" is the same. The farmers did not know the price of grain, and they were full of joy. However, Ye Zijun wrote more and closer to rural life, so the reflection of the rural situation after the disaster is even more tragic. Like this kind of technique, from what he describes, there is no place that is not based on real rural life, which I think is very moving and successful.

With these advantages, there are also many shortcomings. First, what I want to say is the problem of this writer's understanding. That is, in "Harvest Disaster," the author cannot have an in-depth and multi-faceted understanding of the structure of rural society, and writes all the problems as if they exist in a simple and independent way. Second, regarding the younger generation, it is of course possible to write obscurely, but when the obscurity is so great that the tracer cannot grasp a clear outline, the impression that this younger generation gives to readers will be very faint; only with such a faint situation as written last year, in the process of working for the next generation, there is no reasonable, step-by-step development to narrate. Third, in the selection of materials, it is not very appropriate. "Harvest" is a 20,000-word novel, and judging from the materials it collects, it should become a 40,000- to 50,000-word novella, and of course it can be developed into a novel. Putting so much material all into a short story will inevitably fail to have sufficient descriptions in all aspects, making readers feel the crowding and accumulation of materials. However, although the author has these shortcomings, it does not prevent the existence of this novel and its advantages. I express my respect to Ye Zijun.

Perhaps it is because my hope for Ye Zijun is too enthusiastic. After I finished reading "Fire," I felt that Ye Zijun did not achieve the same success as "Harvest" in this novel. This is the sequel to "Harvest," which describes the obscure aspects of the previous article and the subsequent developments. In some places, the impression I get is exactly the opposite of "Harvest." The theme that the author wants to write has not been fully developed, not only losing its organization everywhere, but also failing to grasp the center of gravity in many places. This can be seen from the description of the mass action and the lack of explanation for the arrested people. In terms of materials, if we say that "Harvest" is crowded and accumulated, then "Fire" is the opposite. The content of many paragraphs is monotonous, empty, and lacks truth. "Harvest Disaster" depicts the truth of rural areas, and the author's attitude is also serious and enthusiastic; while "Fire" inevitably shows a non-serious tendency in some places, and the emotions are not as sincere. Here, I feel that Ye Zijun needs to quickly delve into life. I hope Ye Zijun will have better works in the future.

Two Brothers (22) 254

— Written by Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

So, as he walked through the streets and alleys, looking around, he thought about how trivial the reasons that determine our behavior are. For three weeks, he could have, and should have, made such a decision long ago, but it undoubtedly suddenly germinated in his heart because his brother had received an inheritance.

He stopped at the entrances of those houses with beautiful houses or magnificent houses for rent, and he did not bother to look at the notices that did not have adjectives such as beautiful or magnificent. He walked in with great vigor, estimating the height of the ceilings, drawing pictures of the houses in his notebook, and recording how the rooms were connected and the exits of the houses. He told others that he was a doctor and that many people came to see him. The stairs had to be large and clean; and his house could not be located above the third floor.

He recorded seven or eight addresses, and after writing down about two hundred words of explanation in a scrawled manner, he ran home for lunch, already a quarter of an hour late.

As he walked in, he heard the sound of dishes. People had started eating without waiting for him. What was the reason for this? Their family's meal time had never been so accurate. He felt a little embarrassed and dissatisfied, because he was originally very sensitive. As soon as he entered, Old Man Roche said to him:

"Hey, Pierre, hurry up! You know we have to go to the notary at two o'clock. Today is not a day for strolling."

The doctor didn't answer anything. After hugging and kissing his mother, and shaking hands with his father and brother, he sat down; he took the pork chop that had been left for him from the empty vegetable bowl in the middle of the table. The pork chop was already cold and had no juice at all. This must be the worst piece. He thought that people could have left the pork chop in the stove to wait for him to come back and take it out, instead of being so busy looking after the second son that they forgot about the other son丨丨the eldest son丨丨. The family's conversation, which he had interrupted when he came in, continued from where it had left off.

"If it were me," Madame Roland said to Zhe'an, "I would do this immediately: I would live very luxuriously, so as to attract people's attention. I would associate with high society, I would ride horses, I would choose one or two interesting lawsuits to defend, and establish a reputation in court. I would become a rare, non-professional lawyer. Thank goodness, you don't need to make a living yourself now, but you still need to have a profession, just so that you don't waste the results of your research. And a person shouldn't do nothing at all."

Old Man Roland, who was peeling a pear, said:

"Ah! If I were in your position, I would buy a beautiful boat, a pilot's small boat. I could sit in this boat all the way to Senegal."

Now it was Pierre's turn to express his opinion. In his opinion, in short, property cannot increase a man's ethical or intellectual value. Ordinary people will only degenerate with money, while brave people can get powerful help with money. But brave people are rare. If Zhe'an is really a superior man, now that he doesn't need to make a living, he can just express his superiority. But he has to put in a hundred times the effort that he would never have in any other situation. It is not to defend or attack widows and orphans in court, or to earn a lot of money in all lawsuits, regardless of winning or losing, but to become an outstanding jurist, the light of the legal world.

He added two sentences as a conclusion:

"If I had money, I would dissect some corpses!"

Hua Sheng Yu Sheng Ren Zhi Ying Ye (花生與生仁之營業) 275

Peanuts are one of the leguminous plants and contain extremely rich nutrients. Some say that their nourishing effect on the human body is not inferior to meat food; others say that they nourish the lungs and lubricate the intestines, and long-term consumption can prolong life. Therefore, they are valued by health experts. However, excessive consumption produces phlegm, which is a drawback. Peanuts are the abbreviation of fallen peanuts, because their flowers fall in the underground sand before they bear fruit. Also, because their kernels resemble rice grains in shape and also resemble beans, and the shell resembles a bean pod. Therefore, it is called peanut rice or peanut beans. Or because it has the effect of nourishing the human body, it is called the longevity fruit. Those with shells are called peanuts, and those without shells are called peanut kernels.

There are also many types of peanuts. The ones we often see are only differentiated into large and small. Small ones are further divided into those with and without selected pods. Their production areas are in various provinces in the north and south. However, there is very little production in the south because the climate is humid and the soil is mostly sticky, which is not suitable for peanut growth. If the soil in the north is loose and dry, it is suitable for planting, so it is easy to grow. The most famous production areas are Shandong and Henan provinces. Shandong has a large and good output, while Henan is slightly inferior. There are relatively more in coastal counties in Shandong, such as Boer, Weihaiwei, Qingdao, and Yantai, which are even more famous.

The sales channels of peanuts and raw kernels are extremely wide because they can be used as side dishes, made into candies and tea snacks, and are also a good leisure product and children's favorite. The larger channel is for oil factories to make oil, which is peanut oil. Abbreviated as raw oil, its effect is the same as virgin oil and rapeseed oil. What still has a huge channel in the inquiry industry is the export transaction of foreign banks. Try to check the export figures in the Customs Register over the years. It can be proved that it occupies an important position in my country's agricultural products. Foreign banks export selected high-quality products. The bamboo push product area of Shandong Boer has always had a standard: a large grain with 28 grains per tael is considered high-quality, 32 grains are considered mid-level, and 34 grains are another level lower. Er products are mostly high-quality, Weihaiwei and other places have already dropped a level, and the lower grades are , so the price of peanut kernels and raw oil in Boer is more expensive than in other ports. (To be continued)

Foreign silk facts hold , current silk transactions have no outcome, it is said.
